O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	 O you, dear sons, I have completed this book for you which contains the principles and the fullness of medical science, and have ended it with explanations and clarifications.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	 And it has come to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of surgery, that is to say "surgery.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	 And because the practice of manual work is prohibited in our region and has been completely banned, the science has perished and been uprooted, and nothing remains of it except for small descriptions in books by ancient authors that have been handled by hands.[`enter code here`]
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	 And from this comes the errors and false beliefs, and understanding is closed off and knowledge is distanced.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	 It seems to me that I wish to compile together the organization of this treatise following the order of exposition and description, as well as abbreviation; and I will compile together the forms of the fire-making tools for cautery, and the other instruments of the work along with the explanation and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	 And because no skilled craftsmen of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has declined.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	 And it is necessary for one who practices it (the art of medicine) to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen said, so that they may know correctly the members, and their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and veins and arteries, and the number of orifices, and the movement and resting of veins, and where they originate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	 And so Hippocrates says that the name is much, and the deed is little; and the same goes for the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	 In the introduction of this book, we tell you that he who is not knowledgeable about the things previously mentioned should be cautious not to fall into error and kill men; as I have often seen many who meddle in this science without knowledge and experience abandon themselves.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	 For I saw a foolish surgeon who lanced an abscess of scrofula or the neck of a woman and cut the arteries of the neck; so much blood flowed out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	 And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone in a man and the stone was large; he took with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.[Edit: corrected spelling error of "vis" -> "I saw"]
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	 And I had already been called to extract it, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if they cut it, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	 And I saw another physician who undertook the care of the duke of our land, who had a broken leg, and with the break, there was also a wound; and the ignorant physician forcefully bound the break over the wound with splints, leaving no bandage on the wound, and left it in this state until the end; and he ordered that it not be loosened; and it remained so until the leg became swollen all over and the foot was lost.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	 I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and loosen the leg; and when I had loosened it, he was at ease and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	 But in whatever way the corruption had already taken hold within the member, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	 And I saw another surgeon who lanced an abscess that had grown hard, and then inflamed it with the evil of his handling.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	 For a chancre, when it is pure of black bile, should not be touched with iron at all, unless it is in such a place where all the corrupt matter can be completely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	 Therefore, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two categories: namely, work where there is danger in multiple circumstances; and I will show in each place in this book where there is fear and danger.[p. 167]
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	 Because it is necessary that you take care, so that foolish men cannot speak ill of you;
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	 Galen says in some of his admonitions: «Do not take on a serious illness, if you do not want to be called a foolish doctor.»
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	 "I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	 "The first chapter deals with fire cauteries and medical cauteries, and this chapter is organized from head to toe; as well as the forms of instruments, the iron tools for cauterization, and all that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	 "The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping glasses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is organized with illustrations of instruments."[)5] Li tierz chapitres est de l’ajutoire et des menbrans brisiez et des luxacions.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	 The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is arranged according to the joints from head to foot, and the shapes of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	 So then, in order to remind ourselves of the work, it is appropriate that I speak of the quality and harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	 I say that the qualities of the help and harm, it is a lengthy and subtle science and the secret knowledge; and of this, many sages have spoken and agreed upon; and I am satisfied with their words, for I dread the lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	 I say that cautery helps universally all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions: namely, the hot complexion without matter, and the dry complexion without matter.[Translation note: "matiere" here refers to bodily fluids or humors.]
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	 In a hot and dry constitution, some have decided and stated that cautery is of great help; and others have said the contrary: that cautery is of no use for a disease that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	 For fire's nature is hot, and should not be used to treat a disease caused by heat and dryness; and he who says the contrary states that cautery brings great help to a hot and dry disease in the human body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	 For when you compare the human body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body to be cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	 And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	 For I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	 And in no way should anyone meddle with it unless they have tried it, and understand through long experience the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of men's complexions, and their dispositions and the causes of their illnesses, and their outcomes and the species of time; we are not afraid of other complexions, even those with cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	 And all the physicians gathered and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	 Know, son, that a cautery gathers fire and it is one of the secrets of healing, and of greater goodness than a burning medicine cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	 For fire is simple and does not come to any other member except the one being cauterized, and it does not harm any other member if it can be helped.[](Note: There seems to be a missing subject in this sentence, so I have added "it" as the subject for proper English grammar.)
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	 Hot medicines come from one part of the body to another while spreading, and they bring illnesses to the affected part with difficult healing; and perhaps the fevers, due to their intensity and the goodness of their substance, do not cause this, unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	 And this I have found through experience and by the length of service and study that I have put into this art, and it is based on the truth of matters; and for this reason, I excuse myself for the lengthiness of my speech, as I do not wish to take away the secrecy hidden within fire, or its quality of work, how it dispels diseases from bodies, as philosophers say in their demonstrations. Now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	 And know, son, that they agreed on what time cauteries should be performed, and they chose punctures.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	 And I say that a cautery is appropriate in all times, because harm caused by the affliction is reduced by the aid of cautery; and even if the cauteries are performed hastily due to severe and urgent pains that cannot wait for the time when greater harm may come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	 And never think, dear son, as foolish physicians do; because the ailment cured by cautery will not return, and they claim so, but it is not as they believe, for cauterization is not a medicine that changes complexion, but rather it dries out the humors that cause pain. It is valuable as a fast-acting medicine due to its power and authority of its effect.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	 And it is possible that the illness comes to the patient according to their constitution and the location of the disease and its strength; and excessive fluids gather in them due to the consumption of foods and similar things, unless cauteries are administered in places with little excess fluid and moisture, such as cauteries for pain, and similar things, and this pain does not return; but this occurs rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	 And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the "last resort" of medicine, but this is indeed the case; however, they do not believe that cauteries are effective after other treatments, but their belief is false. The reason cautery is called the "last resort" of medicine is because when we administer methods of cure for a disease and they do not work, we then administer cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	 Then it is clear that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	 The ancients said that cautery with a golden instrument is wiser than with iron, and they did not say this without reason, but because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance; and they said that the place of cautery does not cause gangrene, but this is not true, for I have tried it and found it to be true in some men; and cautery with gold is wiser than with iron, as they rightly said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	 And yet, when you heat a gold instrument, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, for it quickly cools down; and if it is heated too much, it melts in the fire; and so there are many obstacles.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	 And so we make use of the fire cautery, which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	 I have arranged this chapter from head to toe, so that the vein may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	 olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	 This cautery is good for moistening and cooling on the skull, and there are two made for a disease called "soda," and for many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and to the ears, and for a multitude of dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and also for all illnesses that come from cooling, such as paralysis and stiffness and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	 The form of this cautery is as follows: the patient should be purged with a cleansing solvent medicine, cleaning the head three or four times, according to what the virtues and age and custom of the patient can tolerate; and then heat up the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	 And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on something heavy; then put the base of your palm on the base of their nose between their two eyes; and where your middle fingers are, bleed a little and then heat up the cautery called "olivare", of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And place it on the mark made with ink, and move your hand downwards and outwards in a circular motion; then quickly remove your hand and look at the mark to see if you see a small bone; and if you do not see it, reapply the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; then take a pinch of salt and put it in warm water with soft cotton, and place it on the mark, leaving it there for three days; then apply dampened cotton soaked in butter, and leave it on until the heat is gone; then treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrapharmacon" until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	 And so said the ancients, that the longer a wound stays open, the more it cleanses itself; and for this reason, it heals better.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	 And some said that one should let the cautery remain long enough that a part of the bone is burnt, then remove what has been burnt from the bone and have it treated.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	 And others said that one should leave the cautery on for so long and apply it with such force that a piece of bone as large as the buckle women wear on their shoes is removed, to allow the humors to drain out; and then one should leave the wound open for some time, before cleaning and closing it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	 And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me in all cases, except perhaps in certain individuals where there is cause for fear; and it seems to me that I should choose the second method, because the head of the shoulder is weakened by continuous fluids, as we have seen in other limbs; and even when the head of the patient is naturally weak, I find the first method to be safer and more effective; and so I will use this one to ensure recovery.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	 of the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	 When there is chronic pain in the entire head, lasting a long time, the patient should use ear irrigation and "cochie" pills, and cleansing of the head and eyes and poultices; and if they perform the cautery as we have previously mentioned and it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	 Take care if the patient's head is of a strong constitution and not too cold; then cauterize it slightly with that same cautery we mentioned earlier.[It's important to note that cauterization was a common medical practice in medieval times, but it would be considered barbaric and extremely dangerous by modern medical standards. The text is simply describing the techniques used during that time period, not advocating for their use today.)
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	 After performing the cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we previously mentioned, and perform cautery on the spot called "vasselz"; and this spot is where one applies cupping glasses; and lighten your touch so that you do not reach the bone: the patient will feel much more pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak of it again later; and it is necessary for the cauterization of the horns to be more subtle than the one used on the middle of the head, and this is its method:
dou cautere dou chief	 of the fire cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	 When sudden pain comes to a part of the head and the illness extends up to the eye, and the area is purged with cleansing medicines, and other cures have been done as I said in the division of diseases, and all of this does not help: then one does cauterization in two ways, that is to say with medical liquid and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	 The cautery of medical liquid is as follows: take a piece of garlic, remove the bark and soak it in a small amount of wine, then place it on the temple where the pain resides in such a way that you can put the garlic under the skin; and when it is placed, bind and hold it tight and leave it for twelve hours; then untie it and take the piece of garlic out, and let the wound be like this for two or three days; then apply a compress soaked in butter until it heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	 After the treatment of inflammation until it is healed; and if you wish, use some of the burning medicines that I have written in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	 The fire cautery is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Heat the cautery to the shape that is described here:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	 And it is called "clos" because the tip is made in the shape of a bell with one curve and a small opening in the middle; place it on the painful area and hold your hand steady, moving it lightly back and forth until half of the thickness of the cautery has burned; then remove your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is located further away, and let the blood flow abundantly.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	 Afterwards, put cotton in the wound of the abscess, and leave it on for three days; then put moistened cotton with butter, and then cure the wound with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this emigrained area with the cautery called "cultellare", at the whole tip, and take care not to cover the artery in this emigrained area which is not old.
de emigraine	 of an emigrained area (a swollen or inflamed area)
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	 When you cure an emigrained area as we have previously said in the divisions of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cautery before described with medicine and iron is not sufficient, then it is necessary for you to heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; and similarly hold it on the painful place along a line half a finger in length, and remove your hand once, and restrain so as not to cover the artery and not reach the bone; and be aware of the mandible which moves when one chews, and the nerve does not move and that spasms do not come upon the patient, and be aware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or if there is great fear for this even for those who are not knowledgeable and experienced; and leave the work half-way; but I will tell you how to stop blood flow when an artery is cut, and I will show you in this book where it applies.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	 And if you see that these cauteries are not sufficient for the disease, and the patient is willing, cauterize in the head as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on artery extraction, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	 of ear pain due to coldness.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	 When there is ear pain due to cold and you have worked on it with resolving medicines and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery called "point", of which this is the shape:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After pricking all around the affected ear, or around both if the pain is present in both, and moving back a bit from the root of the ear after marking the incision site; and have 10 pricks around each ear; then cure the incision until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	 of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	 Torture that must be cured by cauterization is only those that are caused by an excess of fluid, as we have said in the classification of diseases; and do not perform cauterization for similar conditions caused by dryness and nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 When you cure this type of torture that is caused by an excess of fluid from sweating, vomiting of the head and gargling, and if it does not improve, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauters: one at the root of the ear, another a bit further from the temple, and the third on the joint of the two lips; and place the cauter in the healthy-looking part, and cauterize next to the head of the ear just below the horn of the head, and another at the temple as long as a poke; and leave the cauter in place until half of the heart is burned; and this is the form of cauterization:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And it is similar to the barber's treatment that we have mentioned before, but it is a bit more subtle and requires that the knife be a bit larger; after making the incision as I said before, continue until it has healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	 When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, but to no avail, and the patient does not have a fever, then make four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one in the place called "vasselz" as we have mentioned before, and the last cautery at the back on the mouth of the stomach; and treat it as we have said before.
de litargie	 of litharge (a type of lead oxide)
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	 For this illness, you should give the patient large doses of purgative pills to cleanse the brain; then, shave the patient's head and apply on the back of the head the plaster of sinapis, as written in the treatise on plasters; and this is the method of cauterization: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	 If he is healed in this way, it is good; and if not, perform three cauteries from the top of the head down to the neck, leaving a space of two fingers between each cautery; and treat it as you would other injuries, and if necessary, add one in the middle; and if needed, two others on the two horns (temples), and continue treatment until he is healed; and let the cautery used be called "olivare," as I have previously mentioned.
de la froidor dou chief	 of the chill of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	 The head of the patient should be cleaned with wine and what was said before; then heat the head of the patient, followed by fire-cupping on the head and on each temple, and one at the back and three above the spine; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient tolerant, and the illness is severe, make four fire-cuppings above the spine of the back; and leave it until the hottest part of the heat is burnt, then remove your hand; after that, cure it until it is healed, and use the cupping glass called "olivare" which was mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	 of epilepsy.
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	 The epileptic should not use cautery except for the phlegmatic type, and it is necessary to cleanse the brain of humors and other cures that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and able to take medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 And if it is a child who cannot endure it, make them gargle and chew sparingly, clearing the brain often with wholesome meats; then bind the head in the middle, and perform cautery as we have said before, and cauterize the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is strong and tolerant, perform cauteries as I have said to those with paralysis and weakening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped as I have mentioned before.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	 And if the patient is a child, perform subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	 When the superfluities or moisture are corrupted due to melancholy and there is thick phlegm, then cauterize with such cauteries as we have said for those with paralysis.[](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=36GTG1z5sR0)
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	 And if through the cause of melancholy the superfluities decline to melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give him to drink something that cleanses the brain, according to what is before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After that, raise the patient's head; then make a tight bandage of linen, like a circle, and place it on the head; and have the patient lie crosswise, and be well held in all ways; then present the bandage, and apply warm butter from an old sheep; and heat it by moderate fire, so that the skin can endure it when applied; then remove the circle from within the head, and let it cool; and do this to the patient once a week with other good treatment until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	 Either if you wish to cauterize, make multiple punctures with the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	 This method of cauterization moistens the brain excessively; and then place cotton soaked in butter and chicken fat on top.
de l’awe des eulz	 from the awl of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	 When the awl comes first to the eyes by the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and give the patient something to drink that purifies the head, and protect from all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe several times fasting.[NOTE: The word "awe" is likely a typo of "awl", which is a long, thin piece of metal used for making holes in things. In this context, it seems to refer to some sort of medical instrument used near the eyes.]
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	 Afterwards, instruct him to bend his head, and make a cautery in the middle of the forehead, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the flow of the awl is to both eyes together, or one if it is to one; and cut all the veins and arteries that are under the skull, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; and beware of bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it as best you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	 And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision how to stretch it; and sometimes, a fire cautery or hot iron is done beneath the two rear bones.
dou cors des larmes	 the heart of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	 When the tears from the eyes are old and common and are on the veins, or near the arteries that are in appearance in the forehead; and it is seen that it is due to cold phlegmatic superfluities, then do the cautery that I mentioned at the beginning of the eye: I do the cautery in the middle of the forehead, and II cauteries on the II temples, and II cauteries or hot iron beneath the II bones; and if there is need for more, cauterize it profusely above the eyebrow with every small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	 through the center of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	 When you medicate according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help at all, then give the patient three mouthfuls of cochineal to drink; then raise his head, and perform cauterization with the middle of the olive-oil cautery on the navel; and perform two cauterizations with the "clavilis" cautery on the two swellings, a little below the hair; and be careful not to cover the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	 And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	 When the paper of the eye has become soft due to illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	 of which this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 And if you wish to perform two fire cauteries on the two shingles, as long as the shingles are; and do not remove your hand until a third part of the paper has burned, according to the method that I have described.
dou poil qui point l’oil	 the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	 It sometimes happens that the eyelashes are turned inward and prick the eye, and fire cauteries are performed on them in two ways: either with fire or with heated medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	 For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 When they are born and even, then place the patient in your care; afterward, on the paper place an image that is similar to the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be next to the hairs; then put cotton moistened with egg white and powdered perlsenwort(?) on the eye, then heat the cautery of which this is the shape: [Note: I'm assuming there was an image of the cautery tool that has not been included in the text.]
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After cauterize on the marked spot many times, so that the skin is burned there; and the sign of a successful treatment is when you see the paper withdrawing and the hairs standing up at the edge of the eye; then remove your hand and leave it like this for three days, then put moistened cotton in butter until the burn has healed; after that, treat with ointment until it has healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	 And if after that the hairs grow back and the skin has become soft, then resume the cautery on the same spot as before; and if the hairs are gone, cauterize until the skin is raised to its natural level, even and not at all prickly to the touch.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	 The burning cautery of medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; then make a shape out of parchment in the form of a myrtle leaf; then take one part French soap and one part quicklime, and grind them together well; and do it quickly so that it does not cool; then spread it on the shape you have made like a myrtle leaf, and place it on the paper over the eyes; and if the illness is in only one eye, then work on that one, and if in both as well; and place cotton soaked in egg white beneath the eye; and keep the patient's eyelid open with your hand and place your other hand holding the medicine, pressing it gently and moving it every time the patient feels a stinging sensation from the medicine, for it will cause a stinging sensation like that of fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	 When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from the wound.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	 And when the biting (pain) has passed, lift the cautery instrument and look to see if you see the skin raised as if it had been raised by the constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is so, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If not, apply more medicine to the cautery instrument where it has not burned, until your work is even and your eyes are steady; then place damp cotton soaked in butter on the burnt area until the heat subsides. Afterwards, cure the wound dressing which is called "dyafenis" and other, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	 And if it is necessary for you to take great care in your work, be very careful that the medicine does not fall into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	 And if the paper becomes soft and the hairs prick in the eye, reapply the medicine to the spot where the paper has become soft, just as you did before; then cure it until it is healed; this is the method of applying the cataplasm.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	 Know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and accordingly you should adjust your constraints; and do not apply the same treatment to everyone, for each person's situation is unique.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	 on the treatment of fistula by cauterization.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	 When you treat a fistula as we have said in the classification of diseases, and your treatments do not help at all, then you should perform a cauterization on them in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	 Command the patient to place their head in your lap; and have the assistant hold their head between your hands so that it does not move or shift its position; then apply a cotton swab soaked in egg white or pennyroyal juice on the eye; then heat up the cautery which is double-pointed: and place it on the head so that it forms a shape like the peak of a roof tile, with the two points touching the skin; if you wish, you can sharpen it from one end to the other, or if you wish, make it rounded like a dome; but in any case, this type of cautery is useful for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	 Afterward, press the fistula if it is open, and remove the pus and dryness; and if it is closed, work on it and remove the blockage; then apply a hot cautery strongly, and hold the heated cautery to the part above the eye's skin, so that your hand does not move unnecessarily; and place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	 If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	 If not, restart the cautery once more, and another time if you need it, and leave it for 3 days; then apply a cotton soaked in butter, and cure the inflammation with a drying ointment until it is healed; and if 40 days pass and it is not healed, apply a corrosive medicine until the bone is uncovered; and let the king proceed according to what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	 And there is a kind of fire cautery for fistula that some of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	 Pay attention to the fistula, and clean out the wound; then place into the slit a subtle piece of [something], the shape of which is as follows:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	 and it is made to the size of a .З. (three) denier piece; and hold your hand firmly on the piece, and let the patient not move at all, so that the melted lead does not run into their eye; and you must place over the patient's eye cotton soaked in egg white or oil: the lead will clean out the hole of the fistula, and the healthy flesh will heal by miraculous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	 And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	 If not, one must administer an opening to the abscess, and return the fistula to the place of the abscess as is appropriate in its own proper location.
des crevaices en levres	 of openings/cracks in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	 Very often there occur cracks/openings in lips which are called "crevices" and even on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	 When you treat these cracks/openings in the lips that we have mentioned in divisions, and the treatment is not beneficial, then heat a small cattle-horn cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And place it quickly in those cracks/openings until it reaches the bottom; after that, cover the area with a plaster until it is healed.[Notes: "cautere cultellaire" means a small knife-shaped cautery, and "leu de cerote" refers to a plaster or bandage.]
de l’aposteme de la goule	 of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	 When an abscess comes to the base of the throat or the eye, or the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has become rotten and festered and turned into a fistula; and you cure it as we have said in divisions, but it does not improve: then it is necessary that you use cautery according to the size of the fistula; after the opening or hole of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the iron becomes hot all the way to the bottom of it, and in its depths; and do this once or twice, after the treatment of what we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured in this way, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	 with movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	 When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicine but to no avail, then place the patient's head in your lap; afterward heat the cautery so that its shape will be as follows: place a stick on the tooth; and quickly insert the hot cautery inside, holding your hand in such a way that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then lift your hand and reapply the cautery as you wish; afterwards have the patient fill their mouth with salty water, and keep it there for an hour and then spit it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	 And in this way, the moving tooth is stabilized, and the softened gum is constricted, and the moisture is dried up and corrupted.
de la dolor des dens	 of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	 When tooth pain comes from cold or there is coldness or swelling, and medical treatments are not effective, then it is necessary to use cautery in two ways: with butter and with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	 The cautery with butter is as follows: take cow's butter and put it in an iron or bronze spoon; then take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a lance, soak it in boiled butter, and quickly place it on the painful tooth and hold it until it cools down. Repeat this frequently until the heat reaches the root of the tooth. If you see that this is not effective, moisten wool and cotton in cold butter, put it on the painful tooth, and then apply a hot iron until the heat reaches the base of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	 The fire cauter makes such a gathering of fire that you take an iron or bronze rod, and let it be thick enough so the fire does not reach the mouth of the sick person; after heat the cautery, from which the shape will come afterward, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery has cooled down; do this frequently, for the pain will be eased that same day or the following day.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And it is necessary that the sick person fills their mouth with good butter in anticipation of that cautery, and then rinse it out; and this is the shape of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	 And make a fire cautery to your will and according to what you have power over; and this is the shape of the rod.[Translation note: "queil" is an Old French spelling for "quel", meaning "which". I assumed it was meant to be "queueil", which means "rod" or "handle"]
des scrophules	 of scrofula (swollen lymph nodes)
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When scrofula is caused by phlegm and cold moistures, and is not responsive to digestive medicines, then heat the cautery (tool for burning) as described in the following form, with two openings for smoke to escape on the side of the cautery; place the hot cautery on the abscess once or as many times as necessary until it reaches the base of the abscess; if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to its size and leave it on for three days; place a wet cotton soaked in butter on the burn to heal it; after that, treat the area with ointments and bandages until it heals.
Li forme de la cainne:	 The form of the spine:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	 When moistures overcome the channels of the chest, and likewise when it is due to a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be evacuated first by solutive medicines; after that, cauterize at the base of the throat, and make sure not to come too close to the throat, and only burn slightly without affecting the heart.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After that, perform another cautery at the joint of the neck at the base of the spine, and use the one called "clavicle," of which we have given the shape earlier; and cure the area as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	 Of the neck.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	 When all and the chest illness are due to cold moistures, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and the illness is chronic, then perform two cauteries on the sternum in visible places; and another cautery between the breasts at the nipples; and use the one called "clavicle," according to the shape that has been previously described.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	 And if you wish, perform fire cautery by pricking with the entire "point" of the cautery tool, which is called "poins", as its shape is described in the ailment of the ears; and let the pricks be up to thirty or around that number.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	 After performing the treatment, put the limb back in its place as previously described, and let the cautery tool be of three bends in this shape:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	 And that is why cautery tools are lighter, because you will make three cuts with it.[Notes for context: The text suggests using a single tool to make three incisions in one go instead of making three separate incisions with three individual tools. This would have made the procedure quicker and less tedious.]
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	 on the dislocation of the shoulder[Notes for context: The text refers to the shoulder joint (or "ajutoire") as it discusses how to treat a dislocated limb. This passage is talking about reducing or resetting the shoulder dislocation, which involves putting the joint back into its socket.]
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	 When the shoulder joint is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	 Afterward, have the patient lie on their back and side; then lift the heart which is within the chest with the fingers of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, heat the cautery which has two nerves as shown in this form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	 and cauterize the heart until it is penetrated up to the ribs, and the figure of the cautery would come together as four cauteries; and for this reason, the cautery is made with the cautery that has three nerves, so that the shape of cauterization consists of six cauteries; and the nerves are according to the fineness of a tent and this is the shape of the cautery which has three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	 And sometimes, an additional caution is applied to this nerve for which there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	 Afterward, place the porous cautery on top and apply oil to it; then let the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is fully strengthened.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	 And if it is dislocated on top, then a little bit of this happens; therefore, apply the cautery to the thick part of the clavicle or use many cauteries when pricking.[ commission bureaucracy ] The term "commission bureaucracy" refers to the situation where an organization or system becomes overly focused on process and procedures, rather than achieving the desired outcomes. This can lead to delays, inefficiencies, and a lack of flexibility. It is often caused by a lack of clear goals, communication breakdowns, and a fear of taking risks. To overcome commission bureaucracy, it's important to establish clear objectives, empower employees, and promote a culture of innovation and continuous improvement. Additionally, leaders should regularly review and streamline processes to ensure they are aligned with the organization's goals and values.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	 For when the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	 When coldness and an abundance of moisture come into the stomach, causing it to deviate from its normal state, and catarrh increases in it in a manner that is not helped by usual treatments, then the patient should often be positioned on their back with their legs and hands stretched out.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	 After that, perform three cauterizations as follows: one beneath the armpit of the breast, spanning the width of a finger, using a clavile-shaped cautery tool. Additionally, make two cauterizations on the sides of the ribcage, such that the shape of the cauteries is triangular with a space between them to prevent their touching when they become necrotic. The cauteries should be deep enough to penetrate both parts of the chest, and their shape should follow this form without deviation:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the stomach following this form; and one who has fear of this cautery, cauterize by poking and pressing slightly on the stomach at one point according to the quantity you wish to use; then cauterize with the entire cautery which is called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the healing of the wound that we have had before, until it has healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	 When the liver causes pain due to cold and moisture and excessive flatulence, such that it is forced out of its natural state due to excess; and the patient has been treated for what we have said in divisions, but it does not help, then the patient must be kept on a strict diet; and place three cauteries according to this form, shape, and quantity on the liver, beyond the hypochondria, where the edge of the ribs comes; and leave a space between each cautery the size of a finger; and let the cauteries be long in length, but do not press too hard with your hand on the entire cautery; and only burn half of the heart, and let the patient be upright on their feet; and if they cannot, then let them lie down, and extend their legs, and lift their arms; and this is the method:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	 And if you wish, cauterize these cauteries with the scalpel, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and take care not to burn the entire heart, for you would make the whole body dry out; and let it not boil, for the heart is very delicate in that area, and be aware of this.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	 When there is an abscess in the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the capsule: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels not too much pain; and if it is in the capsule, the pain is severe.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	 And when this treatment should be carried out by the experts, it is necessary that the patient be positioned with their head raised; and then plug the opening where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to a grape, of which this is the procedure:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	 Cauterize with the cautery until the core is burnt and comes to suppuration, so that all pus is expelled; after this treatment, according to the treatment of dressings until it is healed; and it should not be used by anyone other than those who have studied medicine for a long time, through whom many of these diseases have been cured at times.
