Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 Then only pierce the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make a fine incision, then put in almond powder, as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a comfortable bed, on which he may sleep on his back in a dark place; and be free from all movements, and eat light foods, and do not move his head to left or right, and bind him according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in that same dark room, and test his sight, and make him look at some things, and then replace the bandage until the seventh day; and it is not necessary to do this during the time of the cure or after the incision now, but rather delay it, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 if pustules appear, let the eye be uncovered before the seventh day, and direct it towards the one who soothes abscesses; and when it is calmed down, let the sight be unbound and placed on its facecovering for a few days, and always remain in that darkened room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And then leave the house frequently, and return to your usual activities; and know that no apprentice should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	 And a man came to us who was from Iraq, who told us that in their country they make almagd perfume, which one can suck up water with, but I have never seen such a thing in our land, nor do I read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	 And these are the likenesses of the forms of hematite, so that those who do not know them may see them; and they should be made of pure tin.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	 And let the tops of them be of the same delicacy, and the rear have three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	 of the flesh above the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Sometimes diverse fleshy growths are born on the nose, among which there are some that resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are such growths that have a swelling of fox-colored flesh, and soft flesh of good color.[NOTE: I am assuming "fuxe" is a typo or spelling variant of "fauve", meaning "fox-colored"]
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 Then for the one that is soft and not swollen, you should make the patient sit between your hands in front of the sun; clear their nostrils and pour oil on those growths and pull them out; then cut what you can hold with a thin spatula on one side, until you are sure that the growth has been completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	 And if any part remains that cannot be covered, open it all with delicate instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if pus forms or an abscess arises, treat it as necessary; and if it is malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize it until the blood stops and all pus is removed, then throw out the necrotic flesh and tissue or use wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If the nose operates and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is healed; and if pus does not drain as it should, know that there is necrotic tissue in the bone above that cannot be cut by instruments: then you must insert a fairly thick linen thread and tie it with your hands, leaving spaces of about a finger's width between each knot; and place the patient's nose in the thread as much as possible, and pull gently while sniffing until it comes through the nose into the mouth; and children often do this in school, and it is an easy thing to do; then hold the part that comes through the nose with one hand, and the part that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and alternate between them while tightening the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Perform this procedure so that you know the wound has corrupted the flesh, then pull out the sutures, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and place it back in the nose as before; perform this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes everything that remains of the flesh; and then place a piece of willow bark on the nose for several days until it is healed, and if drying medicines are needed, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	 And let it be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and lead it in the same way; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be full to purge the head; and have a handle on the head to hold it when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	 of the flesh near the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	 Often, a disease arises on the head of the nose called "telul," and it grows and becomes large at times, to the point that it is visible when looking at it. And so, you must cut it at the beginning and remove it completely, then apply the cautery or a burning medicine in its place. And if you delay cutting it until it has become large, beware if it is hard, of a dark color, with weak sensitivity: do not touch it with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, because when it is cut even once, it can cause great harm to the patient. And if the abscess is of soft touch and not of dark color, and you see that you can cut all of it, then empty the patient's nose and cut it without fear, and cure the place with drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	 when the nerves are cut and sewn up
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when solutions of continuity come to one of these cartilaginous works, it is of little use, except in certain men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, when this happens to someone, look and see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips with a stitch, then cure it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, you must cauterize all the edges of the wound until they heal, then join the two lips with a stitch and bind them, and sprinkle powdered dragon's blood and ground incense on it; and place powders on top of an ointment plaster or another binding ointment, and leave it until it adheres to it, then cure it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	 The manner of sewing is such that you bring together the wound: either with needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	 of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	 To main men, there comes inside the lips a hard abscess, similar to grains of pepper, some smaller and some larger; then you must turn back the lips, and make an incision on each node, and take it with forceps and cut it in every part; then apply the place after the incision with powdered vitriol until the blood is stopped; and then raise the flesh easily, and cure the place with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	 of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	 Often, a swelling of the flesh of the gums arises, which the ancients called "albulus"; you should hold it with tongs and cut at its root, allowing the pus or blood to flow; then apply vitriol powder or other drying and constricting powders to the area; if the flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, cut it again and cauterize it: it will not return after cauterization; these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	 of abscesses or swellings[ISO15924: SMPL](note: this is a guess based on context as "des sordens" does not appear to be a recognized term in Old French)
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	 Sometimes, hard and rough scales form on the top of teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, and become ugly and harsh; and sometimes the teeth turn black, green, and yellow, due to decay reaching the gum, causing the teeth to smell; in this case, you should have the patient sit between your hands, with their head in your lap, and scrape off the scales or loose teeth until nothing remains; do the same for black, green, and yellow stains, and other discolorations, until they are clean; and if all is removed at the first attempt, that is good; otherwise, repeat the process for a second and third day, until everything is scraped off; and know that teeth require various shapes of instruments to be scraped, depending on what the work demands, because the scrapers used to level the surfaces between teeth have different shapes than those used to scrape the tops of teeth; and have these forms and others prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	 It is necessary, when you cure a tooth of its pain, to delay pulling it as long as you can, for this should not be done in any hurry; for it is a very serious matter up until the point where there is no excuse for damaging it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then, when the patient is forced to have it pulled, you should make sure that the painful tooth is the one being extracted.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Often times, the pain deceived the patient, and they think it is coming from a healthy tooth, and they have the good tooth extracted; yet the pain does not go away because of the bad extraction, as we have often seen with these surgeons. And once you are certain about the painful tooth, you should cauterize all around the tooth with a strong styptic to protect the gum from all sides; then extract it with your hands or fine tweezers, pulling gently but firmly until it is extracted completely, then securely fasten the tweezers. And have the patient's mouth open wide and hold it steady between your knees so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After pull out the tooth without breaking it, and if it does not come out, then take any of these instruments and gently insert it on each side, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, you should fill it with cloth where the holes are; and then tighten it subtly with pincers, so as not to break it when tightening; and one must work hard to bleed around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And take care that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, for if the root remains, the patient will have even greater pains than at first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And beware that you do not act as some ignorant healers do, who in their haste and recklessness sometimes break the root, and do not bring about what we have described; but rather cause great illness from the remaining roots or from the broken root, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, rinse the area with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often does, fill the area with powdered vitriol; and if that doesn't work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	 The shapes of the instruments used to move teeth first should be long and thick-handled, so they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	 And they should be sturdy and not bend when pulled, and they should be made of good iron, and have teeth to hold on firmly.
de la racine des dens	 of the tooth roots
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When a root remains when pulling the tooth, you should place cotton soaked in butter on the area for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 until the area is numb, then use forceps called "algefri," which resemble a bird's beak; and inside they should be shaped like a file, and these are the shapes:[As for the phrase "li chiés semblet bec de soigne", it means "the forceps look like a bird's beak". I assumed that based on the context of using them to extract teeth. If you don't want me to add any comments or contextual information, please let me know]
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	 And if the roots do not want to come out with all the pincers, then you must cut open the flesh all around the root, and place in it the instrument called "altthalí", that is, a scalpel, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	 And let it be thick and sturdy so that it does not break, and if the roots jump out using this, it is good; if not, use all the instruments of which the shapes are shown below:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	 And one uses an instrument with two prongs, of which this is the shape:[![](https://i.imgur.com/YKjz4Ue.png)](https://i.imgur.com/YKjz4Ue.png)
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	 And other irons that are before in the reasoning of the teeth, and of this instrument that appears as large pliers, whose form is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	 And let these instruments be such that they cannot break, and know that there are many dental tools; and also other tools, which are not counted; and the wise and skilled master will find his tool by himself, according to what his work and the illness indicates, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach any tool because of their diversity; and one breaks neither the cart nor other bones, or it will rot, so he searches for the tools that are needed, which I have told you, and helps with gestures, whose form is as follows:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	 And let them be thick and firmly set to hold the bone, so that it does not slip, but can hold and remove it; and then restore the place with suitable medicines for this, and if there is rotting in the bone and it is small, use this instrument to heal it.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	 When the tooth appears not in accordance with the body's natural form, and its shape is ugly, and the same goes for young women, you must determine if the tooth has grown in the wrong place and cannot be straightened or filed down. If so, extract it; and if it is loose next to the tooth, use this instrument, shaped like a small beak, made of iron with a sharp tip, to remove it.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	 And the tooth aches for many days due to its hardness, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed down, then file it with a small file such as this is the shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	 And it is like the file used to make needles; and file the tooth lightly for many days with a file such as this, so that it does not move until it heals; then at the end, make it completely smooth with any kind of rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, then file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	 when the teeth loosen.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the teeth loosen, either from trauma or falling out, and the patient cannot chew food without excreting them, and you have treated them with constricting medicines to no avail; then they must be constricted with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the wire be of medium thickness, not too thick or too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to realign the teeth, take the filament and place it double between the two healthy teeth, then insert the loose teeth in between the healthy ones, whether there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin covering again from the starting point, and gently but firmly pull your hand until it does not move; and let the wire be tied at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then bind the jaws with a thread using pliers, and align them, and place it between the healthy tooth and the loose tooth, and position it so as not to cut the tongue; and keep it tight as long as it can last, and if it loosens, or the threads break, then tie it with another thread; and let it remain so and serve in this way all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the alignment of two healthy teeth, and two loose teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	 And when a tooth falls out, it is put back in its place immediately, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and patient, and sometimes the shape of a tooth is made from animal bone, and it is placed in the empty space, and tied as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	 to cover the tie of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Sometimes the sinew that comes beneath the tongue or natural one, when one is born; or by accident of a healed wound; and the procedure is as follows: you operate on the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your lap, and lift his tongue; then cut the nervous sinew wide, so that the tongue is loosened from its attachment, and if there is hardness or knot, and this is due to wound healing, insert the hook and cut wide the knot; and make sure the incision is not too deep, for the artery that is beneath; and when you have done this, lift the area with rose water and vinegar, or cold water, then place beneath the tongue a linen tent; and have the patient touch it every night, so that the wound does not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 And if bleeding occurs, place vitriolic salt on the wound; and if the blood does not stop, cauterize it with a ligature cautery, which is good for that; then cure it with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you see it (the wound) turning into a hard and black color that the patient does not feel, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it declines towards pus, and there is moisture, then apply the oncian (a type of medication) and open it with a thin spatula, and release it from one side and the other; and if blood flows during your work, place vitriolic salt on it until it stops, then return to your work until you extract everything; then lift the wound gently and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	 of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Sometimes a swelling occurs in the throat called "godath," and they are properly called the "two glands." And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is hard abscesses of small size and greenish color, do not touch them at all.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if they are red and the root is thick, do not touch them at all, as well as for the risk of bleeding; but let it be until it softens, and then you will remove it, or it will break open by itself; and if it is whitish in color and has fine roots, prepare the instrument to cover (i.e., lance), but first check whether the hard abscess is calm and at peace.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit down in front of the sun, and let his head be in your lap, and have him open his mouth and the servant place the instrument between his hands, and press his tongue down with all the tool, like this; and it should be made of thin silver or brass, just like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	 And you press the tongue down with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take a probe and stick it in the almond (part of the tool), and pull it up as much as you can; and pull some matter out from the pus with it, then wipe it on the instrument, like this, so that it resembles forceps; and yet the jaws are crooked, one against the other, and they are very sharp, and made of steel or iron:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	 And if you do not have this instrument at hand, take tongs instead, of which this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	 And let one side be sharp and the other blunt; and once you have gripped one of the almonds (tonsils), grip the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with warm water and vinegar, and if bleeding occurs, continue to gargle with water or the peels of pomegranates cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then treat it until it heals; and sometimes other abscesses form in the throat besides the two almonds (tonsils), so cut them in the same manner as the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, that is to say a small abscess; and she had tightly closed her entire throat, so that the woman could not exhale due to the blocked passage, and she could not eat or drink, and she would have died if she had remained in that state for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed out two teeth through both nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 So I acted quickly and inserted a probe into one nostril, then extracted pus and a large quantity of matter; then I put another probe into the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that, I inserted the probe into the abscess and drained some of it, but only a little blood came out; and so the blocked passage in the woman's throat was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut into the abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept growing back and filling up the space that I had emptied, becoming very large; then I tied it off and cauterized it inside her throat: this stopped its growth, and I left those parts, not knowing what God did with her after I left.
de l’uve	 of the eye(s)
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When the rim descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below, large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is healed as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help at all, and you see that the large abscess has subsided, and it is thin, then you must cut it; and the one that is rounded and not long; and it is blood-red or the color of pus or black, then you must avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, regarding its swelling and length, you must make the patient sit facing the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned before; then insert the probe into the eye and pull it down, and cut it at the I of the II instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the II almonds. (Note: "II" could be a typo and should be "I", resulting in "cut it at the I of the I instrument")
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And you should not cover completely the excess (that is) beyond the natural limit; because if you cut more, it will harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient is afraid of being covered (with a bandage), one should use caution with the cauterization so as to not cause fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 And the type of cautery is "ague ague" (not sure about this translation, it's difficult to understand the meaning without additional context).
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And the patient should place their head in your lap, and then press their tongue to the instrument that we mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and moisten it with living vinegar, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and use the tip of this instrument, the shape of which is as follows:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And have a hair or strand placed on the head, such as the handle of a spoon, and place the instrument full of medicine on the eye; and let the patient be lying down so that saliva and muscular movement may carry the medicine from their mouth inside, so that it does not descend to the throat, and they do not swallow it; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the eye, for a quarter of an hour, until you see it turn color and the biting/stinging of the medicine subside; and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument with the cotton into the corner of the eye, so that the cotton adheres to the eye; and do this frequently, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry and fall out after three or four days. And if you need to reapply the medicine cautery, then reapply it, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with cotton in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and cure with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	 This remedy is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take pennyroyal and hyssop and oregano and rosemary and chamomile and almond leaves and similar herbs, and combine them all or some of them in a pot, and add water, and bring to a boil; and the pot should be well glued with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot there should be an instrument like a pipe in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And it should be made of silver or bronze, and one end should be placed in the patient's mouth so that the vapor reaches the eye through the pipe, until the eye is blinded; then start again frequently, until the eye dries out, and take care not to do this at the beginning of a hot abscess, as many things can happen; and do not do it unless the abscess has cooled down.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 And if these instruments are not present, take a chicken wing and put the broken end of an eggshell inside the patient's mouth, so that the patient's mouth is not too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the vapor to burn the mouth, and this is a good cure altogether.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	 Often times, something gets stuck in the throat such as a fish bone or a splinter, or some other object; therefore, you must pull out what you can see, and press down on the patient's tongue with all the instruments while observing if the object moves. And what you cannot see and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit after ensuring that the food has been cooked in the stomach; perhaps the foreign object will come out through vomiting. Or the patient has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a string to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it reaches the location, it will swell up, and then you can pull it out. And if it does not come out through these means that we have mentioned, take an instrument made of plastic in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	 And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it may enter more easily into the throat, and keep the head lifted; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, so that he does not choke, nor push the bone in too deeply; and it is better if the patient introduces the instrument himself, so that he knows where the blockage is; then insert it downward, or draw out the whole instrument evenly, until it is removed.
de la sansue de la gorge	 of the throat's veins
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Sometimes the veins are treated with medicine, as I have said in the division, by means of medical treatment; and when this does not help at all, then look in the patient's throat in the sun, after pressing the tongue with the instrument that I have told you.[translator note: it is unclear what instrument is being referred to here, as no such instrument has been mentioned previously]
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see the vein, pull it with a small hook or delicate tongs that are suitable for this task.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if that is not effective, take a heated poker and insert it in the patient's throat, then apply the tip of the poker repeatedly.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And have the patient drink water throughout the day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 Then take a glass full of cold water, open the patient's mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, moving it with your hand frequently; and as soon as the vein feels the water, it will fall.[Repeated question]
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it does not fall as we have said, fumigate the patient with asafetida using the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.[Repeated question]
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 And the manner of fumigation is as follows: take a pot with live coals, and cover it with a pierced cloth, with the hole for the instrument; then place your fumigation and have the patient put the reed at his mouth, closing it so that the smoke does not escape but reaches the sinuses; and the mucus will now come out, and if it does not, repeat the fumigation several times; and let the patient endure thirst, eating only salty and bitter things, and not drinking water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	 And the form of the instrument used to treat the sinuses is, when visible, similar to bent pliers so as to enter the throat; and it resembles a surgeon's beak, with roughness like sandpaper, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and see the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	 the chapter of abscesses/swellings
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 There are many similarities of abscesses, according to what remembrance comes afterward in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and size; and it is in two ways: one is in its very form, and those that it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second manner is according to the places where they are in the body.[Interpretation]: The second type of abscesses is determined by their location in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 For the abscess of the head is different from that of the anus, and the abscess of the fleshy part is different from that which comes in the joints, and each has its own evaluation in the work.[Interpretation]: The author highlights the importance of considering the location of abscesses when treating them as they can have different characteristics and require different treatments.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And if there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is dead according to its maturation; and if there are such ones that must be pierced when they have grown, and do not die according to their maturation, such as abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 For when abscesses come near joints and are left until they are completely rotten, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint have become corrupted, causing contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 Or if the abscess is near the main member, and you delay the piercing until it is dead, it will harm the main member; or if it is near the foundation, it should be pierced when it is dead; and one must not pierce a grown abscess without completed digestion, except for those near the foundation, so that it does not rot inside and form a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	 And it is necessary that you know the hour of the abscess's perforation, which is when it is ripe according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the lessening of fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the softening and maturation of the abscess's head, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make an incision in the place where the abscess hangs down most, and where it is swollen; and let the incision be long enough for the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places where there is no hollow.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that bend, according to the member. (referring to a bone or joint)
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in a fleshy location, it is better to leave the incision open until it has solidified after complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce it before this, the body of the pus will be prolonged and filled with much filth; and perhaps the edges and depths of the wound will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if there is any abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, depending on what the member needs.[Translation Note: "ceu" here likely refers to "according to this", meaning "according to what has just been said". The text suggests that abscesses should be pierced based on their size and the need of the affected limb. This is a more general statement following the previous specific recommendation about leaving an incision open until it solidifies.]
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And it is necessary that you make small incisions for small abscesses, small holes; and for large abscesses, large holes, and many cuts according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the core and cover it; when it has become as a cloth, and is mortified, then one must do similarly as for boils: and if there are such that are split into three angles, and if there are such where one cuts as the leaf of myrtle, so for abscesses of the shins; and if there are such where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 For those who have no head, such as a soft superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it entirely; and when the abscess is large and has gathered great pus, and you pierce it, then do not draw all the pus in that hour, but draw out some of it; stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more; do this many times, increasing gradually, until all the pus comes out; similarly for those who are of weak virtue, such as women, small children, or old decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the spirit sometimes jumps when the wound bursts open, which may cause the death of the patient, and you would not realize it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Avoid this chapter with great care,
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs during your work, bring cold water and vinegar, wet a cloth and place it on the wound multiple times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the bleeding persists, apply treatment and remedies, and use the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is in winter, and the area where the abscess is located is very sensitive, you should place tents and wet cloths warmed with vinegar and heated oil on top; and if it is in summer, and the area is fleshy, you should put damp cloths soaked in water and oil, or vinegar and cold oil until the third day, as we have said; then unbind the abscess, dry and treat it until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	 And this is what must be generally known in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here comes the chapter.
des soros	 abscesses (feminine plural form)
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 Where small abscesses appear on the head, and they are of two kinds that are like blisters, similar to the hock of a chicken, and there are many such.[**Note**: I have assumed "keur" is a typo for "kieur", which means "head". If not, please let me know.]
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are some that are fatty and have moisture like pimples; and there are those that are hard and stony when cut into, with no doubt that the artery opposes it.[**Note**: I have assumed "artere" is a typo for "artere", which means "artery". If not, please let me know.][**Note**: The translation of "n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire" is uncertain as it could also mean "there is no doubt that the artery does not oppose it", depending on the intended meaning.]
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the operation of the incision (or "taille") consists of you trying every instrument called an "entromissoire", to see what shape it has and what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 For if it contains moisture, they open it (the incision) along its length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture has been emptied, you skin it (the incision) without leaving any of the membrane that contains the moisture, for it will come back if anything is left; then soak a piece of cotton in Egyptian ointment, if available; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, letting it sit until the next day; and those who are on night duty will take care of it.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then redo the cotton, as before, on the second day and the third, until you are certain that it does not remain from night to night; then treat the wound with appropriate salves, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 And if the abscess holds in thick pus, then cut it in this manner, longwise; and throw your leeches thereon, and skin it all around, and devote all your effort to extracting the pus that is inside; and if the artery opposes you, then do as I have told you before.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And do likewise with the abscess if it is hard, and cut into it and cure it as I have told you.[note]: The word "pierous" here refers to an abscess that has become firm or hard due to the accumulation of pus.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And cutting into the abscess pustule and moist area, it is easier, because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if some of these abscesses, either in the head or elsewhere, do not have any moisture, and such as I found in the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess to be as hard as a rough and white stone, which could not be broken; and if one had struck it with something, they would have caused a wound just like from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other abscesses appearing in the head, except those that appear on children's heads and at the roots of ears, the opening should always be in the lowest possible place, so that pus can easily come out; and treat them as necessary.[OP note: The translation for "bowe" is not certain. It could mean pus or other bodily fluids that need to be drained from an abscess.]
des scrophules	 of scrofula (swollen lymph nodes)
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Often, these abscesses occur on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they appear in other parts of the body, and they are large, and are interconnected with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 And each scrofula is specifically enclosed in its own case, just like a knot or abscess of the head, as we have said, and there are many similarities to these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain moisture, and there are some malignant ones that do not want to obey health (i.e., they resist treatment).
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 In the one that you see in good condition when touched, and has a color similar to the skin tone and moves on all sides without being attached to the nerves of the neck or arteries or veins, and is not deep; then it should be cut open from above, and the skin removed from both sides, extending the two lips of the wound towards the incisions if necessary, as we have said in abscesses of the head. And squeeze and press repeatedly, making sure to not cut the nerve or vein, and let the scalpel not be too sharp or cutting, so that the hands do not slip, and do not cut too deep into what should not be cut.[0]
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And if you cut a vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put in the wound vitriol powder, or any powders that stop bleeding, and bind the wound; and leave it until the abscess has calmed down, and the wound has softened and begun to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work until you have completed it; then examine with your skill if there are any small scrofulous sores left, cut and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofulous sore, you should not cut this sore at its root, but instead bind it with a strong double thread and let it fall off by itself without causing harm; then apply to the wound old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then bandage it.[ Anthrax is often referred to as "scrofulous" in medieval medical texts. The treatment described here suggests lancing the boil but not cutting into the root to avoid damage to veins and arteries located there. Egyptian ointment is a general term for various salves, balms, or unguents used in ancient Egypt, often made with ingredients such as animal fat, beeswax, herbs, and resins.]
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you cut out the entire scrofulous sore, it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound and sew it up, since there is no remaining excess due to the size of the sore.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 It is necessary that you attend to cutting the root of it and pulling it out, and sew it up as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Those scrofulous sores that have excess matter, lance them where it is clearly visible; and lance it as the one previously mentioned, by draining it, then apply bandages with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with a running ointment to heal the flesh, until it becomes healed.
de squinance	 of sciatica (a type of pain running down the leg)
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	 The ancients spoke of the operation on the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who performed it, and this is the written record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	 For those who have sciatica, it is necessary that the incision in the throat called "epiglottis" be made; and this cannot be done to help them because all the veins and the windpipe of the patient are obstructed in those who have a hot abscess in the mouth or in the throat or in two glands.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	 When the illness is in the windpipe channel, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis in order to avoid suffocation which comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 Therefore, when we want to split the epiglottis, it should be split below three or four circles, making a small slit across, between the two circles or according to the length of the slit in the syphac, not in the cartilage; and these places are suitable for splitting the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long and slender.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is afraid, he should stretch the skin of the throat to its full extent, then split the windpipe until it reaches the membrane; and avoid cutting any blood vessels, if you see any; and then cut the syphac as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the trachea that jumps out through the broken place, and by the absence of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the hour has passed where there is doubt about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the chest, and stitch it all the way along the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	 Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and the breathing has ceased.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then cut the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and they breathe through the wound, and thus are kept from death; and for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the danger of the illness has passed, and it passes in three or four days. And then they command to sew up the wound and cure it, until it is healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 I saw that a damsel took a knife and plunged it into her throat, and cut part of the tendons in the front; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	 I discovered the wound and found the blood that had flowed from it, and realized that she had not cut an artery or vein but rather her windpipe.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hurried and sewed up the wound, treating it until it healed; and the only thing that happened to the damsel was that she lost her voice for a while, but later returned to normal; therefore I say that in cutting the epiglottis, one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	 of the swollen throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and is a large abscess in color of a lump, and is very common in women; and it is of two kinds: natural and accidental; the natural one has no malice.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the accident is of two kinds, one of which resembles fatty tissue, and the other kind resembles an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and one must not operate with force except in the case of a small one, and test and examine the entire affected area: if you find it like ordinary fat, and it does not bleed on incision, then cut it as you would cut fat, and pull it out completely if there is any; and search thoroughly, and cure it perfectly until it is healed.
des nous	 from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many ways there are, which I will tell you all their likenesses; and now it is appropriate that I say all the difference which is between swelling and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.
