I say that dislocation is heat and fever holding, until the ebullition has passed, and the putrefaction is completed; then the fever and heat subsides.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 With swelling there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins as a small lump and becomes large; and there are two likenesses, either fat or moist, and very much in color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés. Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 And the manner of inspecting abscesses on oneself is to take the moistest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers back and forth, as much as you know the instrument has penetrated the core, according to the size of the abscess; then extract the intruder, and take care not to let it jump out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If moisture runs corrupted blood, whatever color it may have, then lance it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the intruder there is no moisture, know that it is fat, then lance it in a cross shape, and take it with forceps, and lightly flay it from each side and turn the coat where it lies so that you draw it out whole with the pus; and if you cannot draw it out whole, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 For if anything remains there, the wound will come back many times; and if some [matter] remains and the blood bothers you, apply corrosive powders to the wound, bind it up, and place warm compresses on it to draw out the abscess, and treat it with other cures until it is healed; and if the wound is large, cut the two edges of the wound and treat the damaged flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	 And if the swelling of the vein is against you or any other obstacle, hurry and apply vitriol powder, and let it sit for two or three days until the wound festers, and allow the boiling of the blood to subside; then return to covering what remains of the new wound.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 See here the forms of invasive instruments, and they are of three types: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are also three types: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses of fistula; and they are similar to the needles used to sew up wounds, and are made of citrine bronze, or iron, or silver, and the new ones are better, and are proven more effective when dipped in black plumage to encircle the cavities of fistula; and there are three types: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The shapes of the worms are of many similarities, as you can see here: large, medium, and small ones; and there are worms that have two bends of three types; and there are worms that have three bends, and they are also of three types; and there are worms that have two bends, and worms with a single bend, and they are of three types; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The tips of these (worms) that are cut are sharp, and there are some that only cut on one side, so as to scrape the flesh without cutting the vein or nerve; and of the inserting kind are the scalpels placed in handles, so that the patient does not realize it at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three types: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and one never uses them except in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, groins, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another instrument, resembling the shells of pipes, with which to stop blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	 and it is placed at times in a location that heals well for veins and arteries, and sometimes according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 Sometimes the breasts of certain men swell when they begin to become corrupted, until they resemble the breasts of women; and they remain unsightly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them must follow this method from line 2 to line 7:

de la routure de l’artere	 of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When the artery is ruptured and the skin over it is stuck together, often abscesses form, and the same happens when the vein swells and becomes abscessed; this can be recognized when it is caused by an artery because the abscess will be long and deep; when you feel it with your fingers, it feels tight; when it is due to a vein, it is round and visible; and it is foolish to cover such an abscess, especially when it is under the nails, in the corners, at the neck, and in many other places, and it can be very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, one must avoid using a surgical iron and also refrain from using it on the head; for a ruptured artery under swollen skin, make an incision above the skin along its length; then carefully separate the artery from the surrounding tissue until it is exposed; then insert a needle underneath it and pierce it to the other side, and tie it with a double thread in two places as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries in the temples; then apply an intromissory instrument to the area between the two ties until blood comes out, thus releasing the abscess; then clean and bandage the wound until it heals; if the abscess is due to a ruptured vein, then wrap your hand around the abscess and insert the needle under the area you are holding, pierce it and attach one end of a double thread, then tie the abscess as I have instructed with the thread from one of the two ends of the incision; if you fear that the thread may come loose, insert another needle underneath the entire abscess up to the incision made by the first needle, and tie the threads in four places; then remove any excess tissue and leave what is tied; then apply a wet cloth soaked in wine and oil, followed by bandages and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	 of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	 Just as an abscess can develop in an artery or a vein, so too can an abscess develop in nerves when they are wounded, or from excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this happens more frequently in the shoulders and hips, and in all places where there are joints. These are called "shallow abscesses," and their color resembles the color of flesh, and they can occur in various dispositions without pain; and when pressure is applied forcefully, the patient feels pain, but it is not deep within the body, but rather beneath the skin. It can move freely in all directions and does not go forward or backward, nor downward or upward. If an abscess is located in a joint, it should not be covered with a hot iron, as this may cause contraction. If it is located on the head or forehead, it causes the skin to swell.[pw-serve-button text="Translate More!"](/answer/translate-medieval-french-text-line-by-line)
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with tongs and cut into its root;
des grosses boces pendans	 of large hanging lumps/growths
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Sometimes there occur in the belly (stomach?) and nowhere else "thelul", and it is a disease called "funge" because of its appearance, and its roots are fine while its excrements are thick; and they can be small or very large; and I saw a man who had two such funges in his belly, which resembled fungi more than anything else, and there was no difference; and they were white, and had fine roots, and were jagged, and moisture was constantly running out.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I weighed them and found that one weighed eighteen ounces, and the other six; and in cutting into them, you should check if the patient is moist, and the color of the "thelul" is white and moist and has fine roots; then cut it with a broad spatula, and have the cautery with fire ready in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For when cutting, there often comes a great loss of blood, and if the blood flow is too strong, then hasten to use the cauterizer; and if you see the patient fearful and afraid of the incision of the iron, take a well-made flax thread and tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then tighten it and never cease to tighten the flax thread until it cuts the artery, and this will happen without causing too much pain; and if the roots are thick, there is fear of cutting through even to the belly, but you can still cut only half, then cauterize so that it does not come back; then cure the wound, and be careful not to cut the thule which is of fox color and has a poor sense and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	 For it is an inflamed abscess, and I will come to the treatment of the hardened sore soon after.
quant li boude ist fuer	 when the abscess bursts.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of the abscess is caused by a wound or a crack in the syphilitic sore, and it is located on the stomach and comes out through one of the boils, just like it happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries as mentioned before, or from windiness; and if it is caused by the rupture of the syphilitic sore and the release of the intestines, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and open with diverse outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	 And if it is due to the protrusion of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed with one's hands, it recedes and then returns, and perhaps it becomes constricted, and greatly swells at the entrance to the bath and from heavy labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a simple matter, and it is clear when pressed by hand, do not constrain it; and if it is due to blood, then the abscess is large and hard, and swells according to a quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the treatment consists of observing whether the appearance is due to arterial or venous blood, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 So you must leave the wound alone.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 For he has doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, because of the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And if it appears to be due to the intestine or boil, you must instruct the patient to fast, lie flat on their back, and then girdle their belly; then have them lie still in your hands, pass your hand around the area you have marked, extend half of the abscess above with a large hook; then bind it tightly with a strong thread or cord of strong silk, leaving enough slack for loosening; then open half of the abscess while it is extended on the ligature, insert your index finger and search for the intestine; if you find it caught in the ligature, release it and push the intestine back into the belly; if you find pus, drain it with the hook; if an artery or vein opposes you, carefully move around it and then return to your work, placing two needles with strong thread crosswise through what you have pierced; then draw the abscess tight in four places on the needles, and if you see pus, remove the needles and leave the area to suppurate and let the dead tissue fall off by itself; or cut it away when it has become thin and rotten, then treat as necessary, cover the wound, and close it.
dou chancre	 of the chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	 We have mentioned in the division the likeness of a chancre, and how one should work on it with medicines, and how to avoid the cure by iron; and we say that a chancre worsens in the groin, and great caution is required in its care, and the ancients said that when a chancre is in a place where it can be scraped, such as a chancre that is in the breasts, and in the thigh, and in similar places, it should all be removed when it begins; and when it is large and old, one should not at all approach it, for none can ever cure it; nor did anyone ever cure it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the operation, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile once; then make him bleed if there is manifest plethora; then put the patient in a good position to perform the operation; then cast your leeches or chancre and all the hairs from all sides, and remove it completely without leaving anything; and let the blood flow out freely, and wipe the place well with your hand or some other thing, and if the bleeding caused by the incision of an artery or vein is contrary to you, then cauterize it until the bleeding stops; then cure it with another cure until it heals completely.
de ydropisie	 of dropsy (a condition characterized by an abnormal accumulation of fluid in various body tissues)
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 We have said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and how the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: only mentioning; and one should not touch with iron in these two similarities: namely, tympanites and hydrops archis, for it is a deadly thing; therefore when you medicine this similarity of dropsy which is called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not work, look if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as cough and loosening of the bowels and similar things; then do not touch with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other illness but dropsy only, and he is neither too young nor too old, then one should proceed in this way: lift the patient up straight on your hands, and have the minister press the belly by pushing the water to the lowest part of the bladder, then take the spatula spineous according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And be in two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 And have a point, yet not so sharp that it can reach the intestines when inserted, and not be able to pierce it; then look if the dropsy has spread towards the intestines: if so, you must make an incision above the belly three fingers wide right below the navel; and if it is due to disease of the liver, let the incision be on the left side of the belly three fingers wide; and if it is due to spleen, let it be on the right, and it is not necessary for the patient to lie on the incision so that the superfluities do not run to the weak place; then pierce through all the skin with the instrument, and insert it, and lift your hand to leave space between the skin and the abscess as big as a finger or a bit more; then pierce the abscess until the space is reached, and that is the place of the water, then draw it out, and insert this instrument of which the form is described:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And is similar to a thin silver hook, and is made of light bronze or iron, and has a small hole in its lower part; and on one side, there are three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the wound is cut like a feather quill, and this is the shape of the incision that the scribes cut the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 At the top is the albail (a small piece of metal or plastic used to regulate the flow of liquid), so that when the instrument comes into contact with the water, it immediately sinks; then empty half or a third of it, because if you empty more than necessary at that hour, the patient may die from the resolution of their spirit by the weapon, or they fall unconscious, or approach death; but empty according to the amount of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtue indicate, and their pulse; then pull the instrument and retain the water, and it is now retained by the cork that stops up the hole above the syphac (a piece of rubber or plastic used to create an airtight seal), which I mentioned earlier, that you pierce in this way; then reuse the instrument the next day, if you see the patient tolerating it, and pull out a small amount of water; do this for several days, and be careful not to empty all of the water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you doubt the patient, and leave too much water, cure them with sepulture or hot sand, and by sweating or bathing in the sun, and have them drink tanned (medicinal) drinks; and cure them with drying medicines until they are healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	 of the stoppage of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 It sometimes happens that a child is born without an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 Then it is necessary that (the foreskin) be pierced immediately with a very fine awl in this manner:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 then place a thin piece of sponge in the urethra, and bind it and keep it in place for three or four days, and when he wishes to urinate, remove the stopper and allow him to urinate, and then replace it; and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes out will not keep the stopper closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 If his urethra is narrow, then treat it with a piece of sponge as we have said, and it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 Those who do not have their urethra in the correct place are injured, because some are born with the urethra at the tip of the penis, causing them to be unable to urinate unless they lift their penis up; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the opening, and this is a bad illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the manner of the procedure is that the patient lies face down, then extends the head of the penis and trims it to the size of a feather quill, so that the urethra is in the middle, as it should be; and beware of excessive bleeding which often occurs, and if it happens, stop the bleeding as one stops bleeding, and cure the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	 of the pustules on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Often these abscesses come to the penis, and it is a foul appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so one must carefully take them with a fine needle, and cut and clean all of them, then put cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment on it; then cure it with Diafinicon ointment until it heals.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the abscess is harmful, of putrid color and foul-smelling, then you should apply a caustic treatment (cautery).
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 After you have lanced it, and if the abscess is on the penis, with part of it inside the skin and part outside, then you must remove the one that is inside first; and when it is healed, then treat the one outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Because when you treat them together, the opening of the penis is not assured that it will not be pierced again, and blackening and corruption will come to the penis and the area around the anus; then cut away all that is blackened and corrupted, then apply a poultice made of honey, flour, and the outer shells of pomegranates and vinegar, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if bleeding occurs, moderate the lunar causer according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The causer has two helpful dispositions together: namely, in the case of bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then you must insert or guide a reed cane into the penis, and let the patient urinate through it; and when the hairs are dry at the tip of the penis, which happens in those who have not been circumcised, or due to wound or abscess, then you must scrape it with an instrument called a "cheveit," until the ligament is loosened, and release the head of the penis from all sides; and if it is difficult to describe, then you must scrape it with a "spatumile" at the tip of the penis and the foreskin; then carefully separate between two, and place a fine linen cloth soaked in cold water over it, so that it does not become wet again.
de la circoncision	 of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	 Circumcision is not like other injuries in that it is not simply the severing of continuity; nevertheless, when we perform this act willingly, and particularly with children, it is necessary to do the best and easiest work for their health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	 I say that the ancients did not prescribe circumcision for their children, as they did not practice it in their law, and we only have those who we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	 For I have seen that the majority of masters and healers who perform circumcision around the foreskin and forcefully with a novaculum; the knife should avoid the heart because there are two layers, and perhaps one cuts the top layer and leaves the bottom layer.[Original text contains some archaic words or spellings that have been modernized for clarity. For example, "maistres" is changed to "masters", "sainors" to "healers", "faisoient" to "perform", "circumcision entor I dal" to "circumcision around the foreskin", and "novacule" to "novaiculum".]
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	 Or let it be covered, and the pain is doubled, and with the cleansing which is to come, the tip of the limb is not assured; and during the cleansing of the nail, by chance the iron may slip and ruin the work, and many times it happens that there is no need for cleansing and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	 In the cleansing made with force, I have found the goodness of the procedure, for the cautery cuts precisely both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For when you press your hand, you cut evenly in a straight line; but let the thread be well tightened around the skin; and let the manner of the first procedure be such that you make the child think, if they are aware, that you do nothing but tie the thread around the rod only, and then delight them in every way possible; then place it directly between your hands and put the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then place your hand on the rod and blow or cough, and pull it up until the head of the rod is inside; then clean it well of the dirt that has accumulated, then bind the wound with a double thread, then bind it beneath the opening with another ligature; and hold it with two fingers by the second ligature at the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two ligatures, then quickly lift the knife and pull the head of the rod; then let the blood flow for a while, for this is beneficial; and put powder on it and on the powder a cloth dipped in a half yolk of an egg tempered with rose water, infused with good and fresh oil, and leave it on until the next day, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	 The proper form for using forceps in surgery is as follows: the two blades should be sharp and of equal length, and equally wide.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	 The mistake in surgery is when the contents of the abdomen come out at the incision; then you must stretch it to your fingernail, so that the wound forms an abscess; and cut evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with forceps, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	 And if it has been three days, and what is beneath the foreskin is swollen, then leave it until the abscess has healed, and carefully remove the skin; then cut as you are able to move, and be careful not to damage the foreskin, it will not be harmed at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then cure the wound of abscesses with powder, as we have said in the treatise on powders, and if you cut into the core too deeply, and it goes above, it will not harm; so cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	 of urine retention
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 Urine retention is caused by blockage from a stone, congealed blood, dropsy, charnela, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that retention is due to the stone which is in the bladder or the neck of the bladder, then the patient should bend their knees, place their feet on their back, extend their stomach over their back, and restrain the patient's belly as much as they can; this will constrict the neck of the bladder to the expression of the stone above, thus releasing the urine; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you should administer extraction with all the instruments which are called "siringue", of which this is the form: made of thin and light silver, like the feather of a bird; and let the cane be one palm and a half long, and fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the manner of urine discharge is as follows: take a double thread, and tie one end to a wool or cotton rag, and insert the other end of the thread into the syringe; cut off excess wool and push it up to the top of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and seat the patient on a chair, and anoint the bladder and the penis with moist oil, olive oil, and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the base of the penis, then bend the penis over the bulge; then push the syringe further towards the bladder, and let the patient feel it reach the empty space, unless it is done in a different order because the conduit through which it passes is twisted; then pull the thread all the way out along with the wool rag, and let the urine flow; and repeat the process until the bladder is emptied, and relieve the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	 of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	 When ulcers or blood come into the bladder, or putrefaction collects there, and you wish to distill water and medicine therein, do so with an instrument called a "clepsedre", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed and has three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the hairs at the place where the medicine stopper should be such that it tightly stops up the penis without addition, so that the moisture can be drawn out and inserted when necessary; and when you wish to instill your medicines in the bladder, place the head of the instrument in the moisture and draw the string that is attached; so you will draw the moisture into the instrument and then quickly push the string back in; the moisture will enter and go to the bladder, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the subtle form of an enema used to instill the bladder: thus it is.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is made of silver or brass, and the head (noisemaker/enema tip) is higher up; and below is the bladder or the place where the dung falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture in it that you want to use to cleanse the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts firmly with a double thread, and heat one corner of the moisture over the fire; then insert the head of the enema into the penis, then strain your hand on the bladder until all the moisture has entered, so that the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle out of it, and pierce it roundly around; then insert a strong thread through these holes, then gather the circle like a purse, and put inside what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	 of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	 We have previously mentioned in the division the ways of treating stone, and the extraction together with medicines; and I have discussed the difference between bladder stones and all their signs, and in which type of stone one should operate using surgery; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you clearly and concisely.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	 I say that the stone which is located in the bladder happens more often in children, and this is a sign that the urine jumps from the bladder similar to water in its subtlety; and it appears sandy, and the patient urinates frequently, and then constricts; and there are many of these jumps; and the foundation is light in children until they reach 4 years old, and it is very difficult in the elderly, and it is moderate in young adults, those who are between youth and old age; and the treatment is easier for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the cure, one should first cleanse the patient with an enema, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it sometimes hinders the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet and raise them up, making the stone descend to the bottom of the bladder and sometimes come out a bit; then make him sit between your prepared hands, with his hands under his thighs, so that the bladder is completely tilted downwards; then search for it and touch inside; if you feel the stone in this space, then hurry to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not come out upon touching, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is young, or your middle finger if the patient is a grown adolescent; and insert it into their rectum, searching for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, pull on its stalk in the bladder; then press with your finger and push it out where you see fit to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	 And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to lift up the hips with his right hand, and with his left hand move the skin that is under the hips in the area where the incision is made; then insert the scalpel cutting, which is its form.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And make an incision between the hips and the anus, not in the middle but near the left hip; and let it be straight above the stone, and your hands should be always at the level of the anus, and let the incision be wide enough in front and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps by pressing with the hand that is on the anus, the stone will come out without effort; and know that some stones have angles and edges, which makes them difficult to remove; and some are soft like a bean, round in shape, from which the removal is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 At that point then, where there are angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not jump out, you must pull with pincers that are like a file at the top, to extract the stone so that it doesn't shatter; or you put a thin curved instrument at the top; and if you cannot deceive it in this way, widen the opening a little, and if the flesh is thick, constrict it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, first place the largest one at the neck of the bladder, then cut on top, then pull it out, and the smaller ones afterward if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, you must saw it, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 For two things happen to the patient: either they die, or urine repeatedly comes from the wound that cannot heal; but still try to draw it out, or break it up with tongs, as much as you can pull it out in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and place on it a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then raise the patient up by their neck, and do not loosen the binding until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when you unbind it, rinse the wound well with oil and water, then cure it with a diaphoretic ointment and a basilicon ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if abscesses or ulcers come in the wound and congealed blood in the bladder, and urine is retained, which is known to happen without a leap with the urine: then put your finger in the wound and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and cause it to rot; then raise the wound with water and ease and bandage, and help him in all ways you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that during all the hours that you care for him, you bind his two thighs together and assemble the medicines on the spot.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra, and fixed there, and urine cannot come out; then heal it as I said before, that you cut it many times, this is an exception to the rule of cutting.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have proven this before.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	 Take a fork of iron in this form and let it be hammered into three prongs on a stake:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 then take a thread and tie it around the stem below the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then gently insert the fork into the stem until it reaches the stone; and turn the fork with your hand in the stone repeatedly, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon urine will come out, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the stem.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is soon broken and exits with the urine, then the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this because of some obstacle, then tie a thread below and above the stone, then make an incision in the stem between the two ties, then remove it and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure it until it heals.[notes] I have translated the text line by line into English as requested. Please note that this translation is provided for educational purposes only and should not be used for medical advice or treatment. The text describes medieval medical practices, some of which may be outdated or even harmful by modern standards.
de la piere des femmes	 of the stone of women (i.e., a woman's kidney or womb)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	 It rarely happens that a stone is formed in women, and if it does occur, the treatment is difficult and is contraindicated for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a skilled enough woman who can diagnose herself, even when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third way is that perhaps one cannot find a skilled woman in this manual art; and the fourth reason is that the stone in women is often deeper than in men, therefore it requires a deeper incision, which brings great fear. If necessity demands it, then you must take a skilled midwife, but they are hard to find, and if you cannot find one, take a chaste and subtle female healer; and present her with a wise old woman experienced in women's lives or a woman who knows some of the art, and command her to do what you instruct in examining the stone. And look very carefully to see if the woman is a virgin: then she must insert her finger into the rectum and search for the stone; and if she finds it, she must press it down below her finger and command her to insert her hand into the patient's vagina, and press and hold her left hand on the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If she finds it, she should move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder to below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the crease, where it is easy to access, and feel for the stone in that area; and do not move her hand above or below the stone, and make the initial incision small; then push the arrow into the incision, if you feel the stone increase the size of the wound as much as the stone can exit, and know that there are many types of stones: that is to say, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and with spines.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 if you know the symptoms to diagnose the dislocation.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 And if the bleeding persists, apply vitriol powder and hold it in place for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work, continuing until the stone is out, and have the necessary instruments at hand that I mentioned for extracting the stone from men to assist you in your task. And if the bleeding persists, and it is from a cut artery, put powder on it and bind it with bandages, and do not resume the procedure, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, because the patient may die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	 And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the area has healed, return to your work, continuing until the stone is out.[dv365-1e4a-21b0-984c-b8fe3bac75a7] Et quant li chalor est apeisiez et li leus porrirez, si revien a ton oevre, tant que li piere soit fuer.
de hernie carnouse	 of a carnal hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	 Ranice aquosa is nothing but a collection of moisture or white humor, which is under the skin of the groin, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, so that one thinks it is another egg; and this is the skin of the groin that we have mentioned earlier; and this only happens in case of a hernia.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	 And the formation of this ranice is due to weakness that comes to the groin, and this material spreads out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And sometimes it comes from a blow to the groin, and this moisture has many colors: it can be yellowish in color, or without redness, or black, or whitish-blue, and these are the signs for recognizing this collection, because if it is in the white humor that we mentioned earlier, then the abscess is round like an egg, and the groin does not appear swollen as there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the very swelling, it is a ripe abscess with a part of the egg, and for this reason, one thinks that it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the hips and the white of the flank, it is easily felt. Therefore, when you wish to know the color of the moisture, probe with the entire square-ended instrument, by which it is formed in front.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	 Accordingly, judge what is inside based on what follows the probe.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we cure it with iron, the patient must be bled according to their strength and the fullness of their body; then have them lie on their back, on something slightly elevated, and place many cloths underneath them; then sit on their left, and command the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs of the hip bone; then take the scalpel and cut the skin between the hips, from top to bottom, down to the white flank, and carefully peel it back as much as you can; then fully pierce the flank with a wide incision, and remove all the water, and then place your probes, and stretch the flank upwards; and only touch the kidney with the probe; cut the entire side of it carefully, so that if you do not cut it well, the water will return; and if the egg pops out during your work, put it back in its place when you have completed the work on the flank; then bring together the two leaves of the kidney with one stitch, then cure it like other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	 And if you find the eye corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary to tie up the vessels that are suspending, in doubt of bleeding; then cut the connection between the suspension and the eye, and remove the eye and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if the eye has gathered in two parts together, know that these are two membranes; then cut the other part as you did with the first, and wipe away the blood, and place inside the wound wet wool soaked in rose oil; and place on top of it another piece of wet wool soaked in wine and oil, and place the two pieces of wool on top, and place a double folded cloth on top, and bind it all together with a bandage in this manner:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take two strips, and wrap them with loose wool according to this pattern and sew them at the waistband of the breeches, and let one of the strips take hold from the foundation up to the back, and the other at the side of the thigh; and let the other two ends be on the two hips, and let the whole binding be gathered in the loop of the breeches; and this bundle of herbs is sometimes used as a substitute for a knife cut, and it consists of taking one scalpel-like cautery, and cutting the skin of the haunches, and heating it as we have said, so that the white pus containing water comes to the surface; then take the cautery in this form, and pierce the pustule with its point, and flay it with this sharp hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And strike in all ways that you can, until you become fully saturated; and take care that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is safer; and move while being careful of blood loss, and move as in the operation of cutting; and if any thing opposes you, whether it be abscess or blood flow or anything else, then cure what opposes you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this procedure due to its horror, then perform an incision, as I have told you. This means that when you are certain through the signs that we have mentioned that ramic aquous is present, make the patient sit on a raised seat. Then pierce the abscess in its lower part over its entire width, and place the incision along the length of the body. Let the opening be wide, so that all liquid may flow out. Then put cotton on the wound, bind it, and leave it to drain the remaining liquid. Then cure the wound until it heals. And if the white cloth does not allow the liquid to exit through the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a feather or instrument used to extract liquid from hydrops, which has been described before. Enlarge the hole in the wound and know that the liquid will return, and collects after 6 months or thereabouts. And when it has collected as before, the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	 of the abscess of the hips
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the section of this nerve, there is fear in many ways, for which reason it seems better to leave it; and I will tell you about the work and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	 I say then that many abscesses come upon the body, and also upon the hips; and this is due to many reasons.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 That is to say, through the spreading of sharp and humoral excess to the hips, or from a blow; and the color of the abscess corresponds to the color of the skin; and it does not find pain, and is a serious abscess; and perhaps it is an abscess that is fearsome and hard, and of a fleshy color, and sometimes it comes from the bursting of an artery, or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it is due to obstruction of the artery, it is known by the hot disposition of the abscess when you press it with your fingers; and one must not touch it at all.
