Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 A formic is a small defect in the body that goes deep inside, and sometimes one finds it; it feels like death by trembling, and spreads throughout the body, more so in the hands than elsewhere.[Interpretation and translation of a medieval medical treatise written in Old French]
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the procedure is that you take a splint from an ostrich feather, or a strong swan feather, and place that splint on the vibration, such that the circle encompasses the vibration all around; then turn your hand along the entire splint such that you cut all around the vibration, and insert it deeply, and extract the vibration from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	 And if you wish, do the same thing with a splint of bronze or iron in this manner, being fine underneath and thick on top.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	 not puncturing, so as to hold it with the finger and press it; And if you wish, cauterize the vibration, as described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	 of the form of an enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	 Sometimes, a clay or lead enema is administered; and sometimes one uses these instruments, small or large, depending on who they are prepared for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	 Those that are prepared for the treatment of children, and those who are weak and in pain, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	 The shape of a small or large enema is as follows: the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 and there should be an opening where the belly is bound, as you see, and the intestines perforated; and on one side it has two holes, and on the other one; and the belly where one puts the medicine from a beast's bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes, and there should be a space of one digit between each hole, then put a strong thread twisted in the shape of an X or a circle around it, and bind the belly as if it were a belt; and when the medicine is inside, attach it to the instrument with a strong thread, then administer the enema; and this is the shape of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head of the enema with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then insert it gently; then the minister presses it with both hands until it is completely inside, then remove the enema and lift the patient's legs in the air, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it do so as much as it can; and if they sleep through the night, it will be a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you give an enema to a patient with a disorder of the belly, and the medicine quickly comes out, then reinsert it until it solidifies.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if there are hemorrhoids on the anus or a boil, then let the enema be as thin as for a child; and this is the shape of a thin enema where the leather is stretched tight.
des plaies	 of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	 We have previously spoken in the division about the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments for hands and remedies, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	 I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and what they are made from.[
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things by which wounds are made are by the striking of a stone, or the cutting of a sword and knife, or a lance or stick or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and begin with simple wounds of the head, for memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a blow of a stone or similar things, and the skin is torn and the wound is large, and you suspect a hot abscess: then have it immediately cauterized with a hot iron if there is only a little bleeding from the wound, and let the incision be on the opposite side of the injured part; and make the patient evacuate the buildup of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he does not want to be cauterized, then reduce the amount of food he eats, and let him not drink wine or eat meat or any kind of flesh; and place on the wound, if a hot abscess should come, cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in stiptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then place on the fresh wound, with all its blood, and let it not be exposed to air, powder, which I will mention shortly; and if the wound has become inflamed from fire, then place some ointments on it until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	 And if the wound is large, such as from a sword or similar, and the lips cannot come together with stitches, then bring them together with sutures, as I will say for wounds of the belly, by the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound exposes the bone, and is deep, and only holds together by a small amount, then cut it; then cure the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat solid foods, such as heads and cooked wheat, also poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if you find rotten flesh on the skin, and it does not adhere to the bone, then cut away all the rotten flesh and throw it out, then cure the wound; and if there is an artery in the wound or a vein, and without cutting it, it cannot be stopped with medicine, then tie the artery, and if you find it loose, bind it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	 And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is easy: and that is to apply this powder which solidifies once the wound has been heated by the fire.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the way to make the powder is: take one part of incense, two parts of dragon's blood, three parts of quicklime, and grind them finely. Apply it to the wound, holding it firmly in place until it dries out completely and becomes one with all the surrounding blood. Then bandage it securely, but not too tightly, allowing for some movement, and leave it on until the wound heals completely; as the medicine should not be removed before it is cured.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	 And sometimes quicklime alone is used, when incense or dragon's blood is not available, but the wound has already been treated with fire.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the wound has moved to the artery, it would be the same, do not put this powder at all; but apply some digestive ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it dries out; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if a fracture of the bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with delicate forceps; and I will tell you later about fractures of the skull.
de la plaie dou col	 of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	 If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the skull, except if the nerve or artery of the neck is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it is the sinew, there is no other means but to leave the wound alone and not apply any restricting substance, for this harms the sinews and makes them retract; and nothing cold should be placed on the wound, for the nature of sinews is cold, and their connection is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as lime washed in clean water, and mixed with rose oil, and also a cleaned lancet washed in clean water, and other similar stones in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the wound is large, stitch and bind it with bandages, then let the wound heal while keeping it covered until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wounds are deep and gaping and filled with pus, pierce it lower at a different spot; and if an artery is cut and bleeding occurs, tie it off, and bind it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the airway is maintained, so that food can pass, then stitch the windpipe to the ridge of the throat, but do not touch the throat, instead return it to its natural shape; and then bind it appropriately, and leave it for some days, then cure it with discarded ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has left an impression in the bone, seek it out; and if there are pieces of bone, pull them all out if you can, and those that you cannot remove, leave until the wound rots, and the opening dries up and heals; and if the wound is fresh, powder upon it the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	 And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, heal it thus as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	 of the spear or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a spear or knife blow, and the wound is deep, look to see if pus comes from the wound while the patient is lying down: know then that the wound is mortal; but if it is not deep, and the wound is fresh with all its blood, do not apply powder at once nor bind it tight for fear of preventing the blood from flowing and causing it to return to the heart and kill the patient; instead, apply a drawing ointment and bind it twice a day. If you don't have any ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and make the patient lie on the wound for 3 days or 4, or more; this way, there will be no spasms, palpitations, or convulsions. When you see that the bones are properly aligned, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Heal then the abscess and other wounds, until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, know that there is a fistula; heal it as it should be done.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, whether on the belly, side or back, heal the part in front; if it is large, with sutures; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is close to the bone, and there are pieces torn off, then clean the wound, and pull out the fragments if they are separated; and if they are not separated, then let the wound rot, this will make the extractions easier. And for other wounds in other limbs, judgement is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	 rupture of the belly/abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The rupture of the belly is large, medium, and small; from a large wound sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines come out, causing their insertion; and suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because the intestines are more difficult to put back in, if they are not put back in place hot against hot; for the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, and therefore it is better to reset them with movement, because the intestines return to their place more easily, and therefore a medium wound is preferable, because the intestines can be reset in their place more easily than other parts of the body; and know that there are four types of abdominal ruptures: two common sutures occur in the abdominal suture, and two other common sutures occur in other bodily wounds, but they are more specific to the abdominal suture; and I will describe each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestines protrudes, and it is difficult to put back, it can be done in two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, warm it in the following way: wet a sponge or a piece of cloth in warm water only, or cook it in a decoction of wormwood, cypress, and pepper, and sprinkle the intestines until the swelling is removed; and sometimes use this wine to restrain, and it is often effective in reducing swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling subside, moisten the intestines with water or broth of herbs that are alexiteric (against poison), for this facilitates entry; and if it cannot enter, make an incision in the wound with the instrument used to cut piles (hemorrhoids); and the first treatment is more effective when little is removed, and one should not cut unnecessarily; and this is the shape of the instrument: [Here provide a sketch of the instrument].
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is opened and the intestines come out, put them back in their natural shape and proper place, if you are able to, for it is worth more to move them.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is large and it is in the area below the belly, you should have the patient lie on their back and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the area below the belly, place the head and chest higher than the parts below, and do the same if the rupture of the belly is in one of two parts, make sure that the wounded part is higher than the other; and you should manage what I am saying in both large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 Small wounds, use what you have prepared;
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I set the intestines back in place after they had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed over the course of fifteen days, and I treated it, and it was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And the doctors had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine; and I placed clean old cotton on the wound two times a day, and washed it with honey water until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 I will tell you the two proper methods of stitching: take the needle and insert it from the outside in; when it has pierced straight through, leave the tip of the siphac or thread on that side, and make it come out the other side from the inside out; and the technique of this stitch is such that you sew like a pelterer does leather, leaving a loop of the siphac on one side and taking it up again on the other, until the stitching is fully completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second manner of stitching, which Galen properly calls for, is as follows: some bring the two parts together naturally and apply one chief part of the suture to the other in such a way. First, insert a needle or chief part of the suture close by, and only pierce that place, leaving the two edges of the wound; then turn the needle and make it pass from the outer part to the inner part, through the two edges of the wound; then make both the outer and inner parts pass through, in two other holes of the suture on the other side; and this is the true manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galen says this word, and some testify to it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, with thread in each; and one should insert one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew leather; and know that when the tear is in the middle of the belly, the sewing is more difficult than at other places on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgment of the wound is as follows, just like the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh, with all its blood, so that the air has not moved it, then replace the intestines and sew the cut; then put powder on dried flesh, and if the air has moved it, then put on some available ointment while the wound is still open; and moisten the thread, and let the sutures and the wick be sealed; then cure the wound as with others, until it heals; and if you don't have medicines, then put on old cotton, as soon as it begins to close, and move it two times a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 For you do not need any other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound may communicate with the principal members, then it is necessary to moisten thin linen in oil of tempered heat, or in rose oil, and place it around the edges, and beneath the buttocks; and if he feels pain or corruption in the belly, and this often happens, then purge him with warm black wine, and similarly if the corruption comes as far as the intestines; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine that is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is due to the multitude of veins that are there, and the delicacy of the entire body, and its proximity to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the worm exits the wound, put it back in place as you would the intestines, while it is still fresh; and if it is old and turned black or green, tie off the blackened area to prevent bleeding, for there are veins and arteries there; then cut out the part that is between the tie and let the two ends hang down from the part beneath the wound to lighten the extraction when the worm exits, and let the wound swell.
de la routure dou boueil	 of the opening/hole of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestines are cut and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, because I have seen that a man was wounded with a lance in the abdomen; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and became inflamed and developed into a fistula, and there came out excrement and gas; I treated it as best I could and did not stop until it healed and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I saw it soldered, I feared that the patient would have pain in his belly; and he had no such pain, but rather improved in condition, eating and drinking; and some experts said that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be bound in this manner: take large bandages, then bring the edges of the wound together, and when the bandage has opened its mouth, place it on top of the two edges so that it pulls the edges toward itself; and then cut off the head of the bandage, and this will hold so that it cannot become loose, then place another bandage in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely covered; and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 The head of this instrument is heated in the interior, and it brings no harm to the patient, and one can bind the interior with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in such a manner: take the head of this intestinal filament, which is very stripped of flesh, and then bind the head of this filament to a thin twisted linen thread, then insert the thread into the needle and sew the intestine, and pull it tight at the opening; and this method of suturing is not outside the path of trust and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no means or cure, except for delicacy.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	 of a fistula or where it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that any wound or abscess, when it matures, is universally called a "fistula," and likewise when it heals and becomes sunken.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And a fistula is, according to its true nature, a hard and white swelling that is not painful and is sunken like the feather of a bird; sometimes it is clear and hollow, other times thick; sometimes shallow, other times deep. I have previously spoken in the division of wounds, that any wound that has not healed, and there is no flesh, this is not due to anything but one of the Nine causes: namely, by the small amount of blood or tissue; or because of its malice; or because there is hard scar tissue inside and on the edges, which does not allow for flesh to grow; or there is too much hollow space; or the area is putrid, and the material is of poor quality; or the medicine used in treatment is not good; or due to the corruption being a type of pestilence; or due to the nature of the region being slow to digest and heal, causing it to swell; or there are veins or bones. I have already shown all these causes, signs, and cures using medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	 And it is necessary for me to make known to you the treatment of a fistula which is made by handiwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that a fistula can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from the great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the syphilis, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to some joint of the hands or feet; and there are those that come to the very nature of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all fistulas of this kind are of difficult healing, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I mentioned, and you have faith in the cure, and you wish to recognize it, take a probe of iron or of steel, if the fistula is straight, seek it out; and if the fistula is twisted, search for it with a subtle probe of lead, for lead easily bends around the twist. And if the fistula has many holes and you cannot find it with probes, irrigate it through one of the holes, for moisture quickly travels from one hole to another, and cleanses it; then seek it carefully as best you can, so that you know whether there is bone or nerve involved, and if it is embedded deep within. Ask the patient carefully about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and where they feel it. And when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or any of the places I have mentioned, then proceed according to what I have said, and remove the abscess and the corrupted flesh that is inside; and then cure it until it is healed. And if the fistula is deeply embedded in a straight direction, you must cut deeply as far as you can, then apply moist bandages soaked in medicine, pushing them up to the top of the fistula, until the medicine dissolves the remaining excess material at the bottom; and then apply healing ointments until the flesh has healed. And if it is not healed by this method, cauterize it as we have said. And if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If vein or nerve does not trouble you, nor the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, let the king (a type of medieval surgical tool) touch it until all corruption is removed, then cure the wounded flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and returns to its former state, know that you have not yet reached the bottom: uncover and search until you reach the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore the place; and if it is healed in this way, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot reach it; there is no other device but to leave it to nature; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it with tongs, then pull it out with a suitable instrument for this, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, do not leave any; and if moisture (pus or infection) opposes you, and there is no error or fear, cut away the moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place something foul-smelling on the wound to promote putrefaction, and leave it until the area around the bones has rotted; then the bones will come apart more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh bone, then simply allow the corruption to progress until all the blackness is gone, then restore the wound; but if a large part of it has corrupted and has reached the marrow of the bone, then it must be covered and sealed until the corruption is healed, and then cure it until it has healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and aid from it in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 A young man of about thirty years old had pain in his leg due to an internal cause, such that matter came into the leg and caused a large abscess, and there was no obvious reason to open it; but the physicians, out of their folly, operated on the abscess so much that it opened and a great deal of matter ran out, and it became a fistula, and a lot of pus came out, all of which stank; and many physicians applied treatment to it for two years, and there was no skilled person in the art of medicine among them, until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and the matter that was running out through the openings, which were very large; and the young man's skin became red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I pitched a tent in one of these openings, and then examined all the openings, and found that one came toward the other from all sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 I hurried then, and cut into one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the rot reached to the bone inside; I thought what appeared of the rotten bone was all of it, and believed there was no other corruption except that which I removed; and I began to treat the wound with soaking medicines for a long time, but it would not heal; and then I tried again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I removed what appeared of it, and then I extracted more, and took great care to heal the place; but I could not do so until I cut around a palm's width of the bone, and pulled out all its marrow, and then healed it with medicines; and it was quickly healed and sealed, and there was no need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it, and my fear of his death.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 For through the evacuation of blood, he often sweated, but he was completely healed, and in place of the bone, hard flesh grew, and it was of good disposition and caused no harm or contrary effect at all, neither when going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this way: take a bandage and strain it at the end of the bone that is visible, and command someone to stretch it upwards; and place another larger linen bandage over the skin that is above the bone, and stretch it so that you pull the rotten flesh underneath, and uncover the flesh above the place where you want to operate, so that the bandage does not cut or wound the flesh; and place a piece of wood or a board beneath the bone to cover the rotten flesh; and it is necessary to continue operating until one can see and feel that the corruption has been removed, and to operate again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 And if the bone is corrupt and not visible, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, reveal all the flesh; then place a piece of ember underneath, and then cover the corruption with thread from one side to the other, and make the thread a finger's width away from the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut the corrupt joint and cover the bone or what it contains on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other option but to cut; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand, or in the ankle of the foot, this is a very strong thing, but nonetheless you must examine the corruption, how it appears to you; and cleanse it in all ways that you can, but without letting the vein or nerve prevent you; and know that the knives and threads for cutting bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and fineness, and their size; and therefore it is necessary to prepare a specific tool for each type of work; and know that the task will show you the tool that you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so consider the tool that you need according to what is required.
dou feu	 of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The shoulders rot or corrupt both from within and without; and when you have treated this corruption with the cure of medicines, and it does not improve, then you must cover that member up to the place where the corruption reaches, so that the patient escapes from death, or from the greater evil, which is the defect of the member; and the sign of this is that the member becomes black, as if it were burnt by fire, and will corrupt afterward, and then this corruption spreads from member to member, taking hold of the whole body; so you must hurry to cover it, and if it is due to the sting of any venomous beasts, such as a sea scorpion and a viper and similar ones, if the corruption is in the hand, then cover it, and do not give it space to reach the arm.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it reaches the hand, it seizes the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, it cuts with the knife; and if it surpasses the knife, it is death, and no medicine but the amount of its strength helps; and it acts in this way whenever the corrosion comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then it seizes after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, then it cuts all the foot; and if it rises in the leg, then it cuts at the joint of the knee; and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other means but to let the patient die; and the way of cutting or sewing the member is that you tie it above and below, and stretch out a suture on one side of the ligament downward, and another suture on the other side upward, and you separate the flesh which is between the two ligaments to the width of one span, so that the bone is exposed; then cut or sew, and place a linen cloth on each side, so that the suture does not touch the healthy place, and comes to the patient no other harm and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 And if bleeding occurs while you are working, then cauterize the area quickly, or apply tightening powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you of an occurrence with a man: he had a discoloration that resembled burns from fire, and this corrosion first appeared on his foot's toe, to the point where it spread throughout the whole foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he quickly covered his foot and was healed; and long after, the corrosion returned to the toe of his hand, and he came to me, and I applied reactive substances after cleansing the body, but the corrosion could not be stopped; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not, as I had hope of reversing the matter; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, as the man's strength was weak; and he gave up all hope, and returned to his land, and quickly covered his hand, and was healed; and I have only told this story so that others may do the same if necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 Sometimes a abscess comes in the groin area, and remains so long that it makes a large collection of pus; and then it breaks and pierces, and the pus drains out, leaving the wound open, like a vessel; and the skin that is on top is as thin as delicate fabric, and does not extend all the way to the bone, nor to the nerve. Such a disease is called "sain", and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so elongated that it reaches the bone deeply, it is then called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you can cut it all around, and likewise when it is thin, as with delicate fabric; and it does not heal easily due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est. Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement. Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	 And if the breast sinks down and becomes engorged after many days, know that the breast is not healthy.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle venoms come out after a long time, do not lose hope for health, because health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 For there are men who have delayed healing of flesh in their wounds, and those who do the opposite; and if the breast sinks down and becomes engorged after many days, know that the breast is not healthy; and if the breast takes a long time to heal, and is far removed, apply drying medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diaphoretic ointment, for there is a great part of vitriol in it, and it is the last medicine; take diaphoretic ointment, and mix it with rose oil, and add equal parts of old wine in substance; then cook it and use it; and if increased swelling occurs when diaphoretic ointment is not present, or you take myrrh, aloe, and incense, grind them, and sprinkle the powder on the honey while it is still on the fire; then wrap it in glue and apply a plaster to the breast, and sometimes administer longwort and lily root, which is also known as vetch flour and centaury; and use simple or compound remedies: grind them and make a powder, and put it on the honey that I mentioned earlier, and use it; and if the cure takes a long time and is not cured by this cure, then know that corruption has reached deep within, causing pressure on the bone, or in hard members or ligaments; in this case, use the cure for fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	 of the abscess of the nail (toe/finger)
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 Panaritium is an abscess that arises under the nail of the finger or foot, and sometimes it may arise in other places; and when it has grown old and not taken care of, then a foul abscess comes, and it runs and spreads until it reaches the root of the nail, and possibly corrupts it all; and the corrosion reaches the bone, so that there is painful stinking pain, and the finger becomes wide with a blackish color.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you cure it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all, then you must cut away with iron all the remaining excess from under the nail, then cauterize the wound after.[ safe certification training](https://www.safeandsurecertification.com/training-programs/)
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The cautery is a great help if the bone is sound, and the nail is healthy; and if the nail approaches the flesh and begins to prick, and injure it, you should place a hot iron below the nail to stop it from piercing the flesh, and lift it up, and carefully and lightly cut away that bit of flesh, and apply heated medicinal drugs on the remaining flesh to remove all [of it]; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it out and remove it, for as long as there is decayed bone present, it cannot heal; and if you see that the wound is becoming corrupt, cut it in the shape of a nose as described earlier, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is pierced and protruding and causing great pain, first clean the wound; then cut the toenail lengthwise, taking care not to cut all the way down to the flesh beneath the nail, for this would cause too much pain; and if necessary, place something soothing on it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	 the pain that arises from the wrist
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The two swellings that sometimes occur in men's hands by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there are some where there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and some of them are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in one of the fingers of the hand.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 The one that is born in any knot of the finger does not move, and the one that is born at the joint of the finger, by chance moves; the size of the fleshy one is small, in such a way: cut it at its root with a broad spatula.[ burned at the root with a large spatula.]
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	 The one that is born in the root of the joint is difficult to cure: hold it under the cover.[ keep it covered.]
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the one who is born or will be born with a tight foreskin, you should first cut the skin roundly up to the bone, then cut the bone to an appropriate thickness, and then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	 The swellings that come at the joining of bones come from birth, or from the healing of a wound, or from burning with fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 You should cut the swelling so that the parts come together according to their natural shapes; then place between them two tents or damp cloths soaked in oil, so that they do not join together again; or you can place two thin pieces of wood until the area is healed as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	 If swelling comes to one of his two hands with the palm, cut open that swelling as it should be done.
des vils	 of the common people
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 Veins are large vessels full of melancholic superfluities, which come to many members of the body; and this happens more often in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	 Therefore, you should administer purging of bile to them, and then treat them with basilicum (a medicine made from various plants).
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The treatment with a knife is done in two ways: one way is to cut (the vein) and let out the black blood; and the other way is to open the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The incision is done in the following way: first, apply very hot water to the leg until the swelling subsides, then tie the leg of the patient from above the thigh down to below the knee; then cut the vein in one place or two or three places with a wide incision, raise (the affected part) and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the strength of the patient can bear; then bind it up and tell him to eat foods that provoke yellow bile; and start the evacuation and bleeding again when the veins are full, and this harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The treatment of this is as follows: raise the patient's leg if there is a lot of hair, then place it in a bath and apply warm water to the leg until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it by the fire. Then make an incision along the long vein at the top of the knee or below the ankle; then pull back the skin with a lancet and cut the vein from both sides until it is visible when touched; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord. Then insert the stylec (a surgical instrument) under it until it is raised from the skin, then gently pull on the lancet, then make another incision above or below as needed. Then lift the skin above the vein until it is visible, then raise it with the stylec and pull it with a lancet as before; then make another cut, or several if necessary, then lift it and pull it to the second cut; then extract it vein section by section until it comes out completely, then close (the wound). And if you cannot pull it out and lift it, insert a needle with strong doubled thread and tie and pull it, and insert a stylec under it, and turn your hand back and forth until it comes out; and be careful not to cut it, for if it is cut, it cannot be pulled out or lifted, and this will harm the patient. And when you have completely extracted it, place wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound and care for it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the eye sight is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you should split it crookedly, but do not cut it; and pull it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The shape of the iron with which you cut the eye should be curved and not straight, so as not to cut the vein; and it should be of thick curvature, because if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein runs in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in ground that has no moisture; and it may perhaps arise elsewhere than in legs, and this happens due to decay that comes from under the skin, as a snake or worm crawls between the skin and flesh.
