Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this ailment are that there comes to the leg a very great inflammation, then the area changes color and the wound begins to ooze out like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the wound is open, you should wrap it with a piece of linen cloth from 3.5 to 4 inches wide, and tie it in place. Leave the cloth hanging from the leg. Each time it protrudes, wrap it again with the cloth and tie it; if it is too long, cut off part of it but do not cut it at its root until it has fully emerged. If you cut it before it is fully out, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess or decay in that place, leading to a serious illness. Therefore, it must be treated carefully and thoroughly, leaving no remnants in the body. Sometimes this wound can be as long as 5 or 10 palms, and I have seen some cases where it was even longer. When cutting it, make an incision with one finger's width and depth until it is fully drained, and then apply healing medicines to prevent decay. Then treat it like an abscess.[no comments]
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes at this vein (there are) many flows, and even when it appears in the joint of the foot or hand, and there comes a lot of bleeding, and then it sprouts again; then cure it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This disease is called in our land "maladie de buef" (ox disease), because it often occurs in oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and it moves throughout the body going up and down, and one can feel its movement from member to member, until it breaks the skin where it goes, and it comes out; and it is generated from the putrefaction of certain humors, such as worms, snakes, larvae, and ascariasis in the belly; and there is fear of its harm, because when it moves through the body and goes up to the head, and reaches the eye, perhaps it enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see it being cured and pulled, it is impossible for it to go without moving: therefore, you must tie the area above and below with a strong, tight ligature; then cut and pull it out, and if the wound goes deep into the flesh and you can't find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it can do is to run to the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the head, near the eye, firmly press down on the eyelid, then cut and pull it out; and the patient should use purifying medicines for the body to remove harmful humors, and beware of corrupting foods that cause rotting.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that appears in certain limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and shortly after, I saw it growing like a worm to the shoulder, more quickly than any other thing, like quicksilver when it flows from place to place; the pain departed from that place and fixed itself in the shoulder, and then soon spread throughout her body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that it turned around her body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	 I marveled greatly how it moved thus from member to member, for I had never seen this disease presented in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 Nevertheless, I had seen many times that people could move pain from one place to another, but I had never seen it presented in such a way as I did with the woman; and I thought that this must be due to the fact that women have dry bodies and exposed veins, and for this reason, these wind-like disturbances are apparent; and this is not noticeable according to this reasoning in those who are overweight, and who have moist bodies and veins which are not prominent.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And when you see this disease and the patient feels the pain, if it appears as we have described, then press on it strongly both above and below, and continue to do so until the wind-like disturbance is forced out of that place; and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it with your own eyes, then treat it with those remedies which are used to alleviate wind-like disturbances, such as stinking pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	 of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	 Arrows are diverse, according to their shapes and according to the parts of the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 The diversities of their tips are that there are some with large points, small ones, barbed and blunt; and some have two angles, and some have tongues, and some have pieces; and an arrow that lands in a limb does so in two ways: either it lands in a principal member such as the head, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it lands in any part of these members and the signs of death that I will tell you appear later, then you must be careful with extracting this arrow because death follows in many dispositions; and when these bad signs do not appear and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then extract it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And the sign of the brain when an arrow falls and pierces the bone, and the dura mater that is above the brain shifts, is when there is scotoma (a blind spot in vision) and numbness and dizziness and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and a mixture of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there is discharge of pus from the nose or ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice; and there is an exudate from the wound, white and resembling curdled milk, and it also oozes as if a lump of flesh has been torn off; and if these signs appear to you, then refrain from treating and pull out the arrow if it is not already in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The signs of an arrow wound when it hits the heart are: it is close to the left breast, and it feels as if it is stuck in something hard, not hollow; and perhaps the arrow moves like a bird's wing, and there is a flow of dark blood, and chill sets in, causing cold sweats and fainting: then know for certain that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	 And the signs of an arrow wound that does not reach the chest are: it spurts out foam without blood from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	 And if the arrow falls on the covering of the lung, it is next to the ribs; and causes great pain and suffering, and difficulty breathing, and trembling in all members of the shoulder.[Note: I am assuming that "coverture dou pis" refers to a part of the body related to lungs, if not please let me know]
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	 And if an arrow falls into the stomach, perhaps some undigested matter may jump out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	 And if an arrow falls into the belly, and some feces jumps out through the intestines, there is no hope in the treatment or in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	 And if an arrow falls into the bladder, and urine jumps out and comes out, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is fatal.[ editorial note: "jumps out" in this context means that urine flows out from the wound]
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	 The other limbs, such as the arms and neck and throat and shoulders and spine of the back and ribs and hips and legs, and similar members, are safe according to various conditions.[ editorial note: "according to various conditions" likely refers to factors like alignment, injury, or illness that could put these body parts at risk]
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	 When an arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you can do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 It happened to a man that an arrow struck him in the tear duct at the root of the nose: I pulled it out and extracted it from the other side under the ear fat, and he was healed without trouble.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And I extracted an arrow that struck him in the fat of the eye beneath the eyelid, and the arrowhead was embedded, and I could not reach it but for the tip pointing towards the inside, and the arrow was large from a Turkish bow, all iron without ears; the man was healed, and no harm came to him.[Notes: This translation is based on the assumption that "jeus" in the original text is a misspelling of "jeu", meaning 'man'.]
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And pull an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with feathers: I saw the beard, and skillfully pulled it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And pull an arrow from a man, who had it fall in his belly, and I thought he would die; and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change. I cut at the arrow, extracted it carefully, pulled it out, and he had no adverse effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And if you want to treat a man who has an arrow stuck in his back and the wound has healed over, but the arrow remains inside him and does not affect his natural condition or cause harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 And see another man, to whom an arrow fell in his face, and the wound was healed; and he remained without suffering great pain; and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 And I pulled an arrow from a man of the prince's, which had fallen in his nose, and it was slanted towards the right side; and the arrowhead was completely buried. I was called to the care after it had been there for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 I probed it with a thin probe and felt nothing; and he felt pricking and pain under his right ear.[ ](https://llmmyy.github.io/)
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was the tip of the arrow, so I applied a plaster of artractive and digestive ingredients to the area, in order that the wound would not swell; and the place where the arrow was appeared.[ ](https://llmmyy.github.io/)
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 I applied the poultice for many days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained in this state for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his nose; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 I put corrosive medicine on the wound for many days, until it was open, and I probed it, and felt the tip of the arrowhead lodged in place; then I introduced the corrosive medicine into the opening of the wound, until the head of the arrow became visible to me; and more than four months had passed when the wound began to heal so that I could introduce forceps, both sides of them, but it could not come out; then I did not stop trying and devising various methods of instruments, until one day I took it with well-made forceps, according to its shape which will be described at the end of this chapter, and pulled it out, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the surgeons deemed that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I then restored it, and the wound was healed, and the patient was fully cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 I have told you the nature of extracting certain arrows, so that you may apply your skill to what I do not mention, for a book cannot grasp everything; but a wise master can compare even a small thing well, and find new methods and tools for dealing with unusual occurrences in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows do not exit the members they are lodged in except by two means: either through the place where they entered, or through another part; and those that exit from the same place they entered are flesh-wound arrows, which sometimes exit at once.[](https://www.deepl.com/translator#fr/en/Je%20dis%20que%20les%20saiettes%20n%E2%80%99issent%20des%20membres%20ou%20elles%20sont%20fichies%20fuer%20que%20selonc%20II%20manieres%3A%20ou%20par%20lou%20leu%20ou%20elles%20entrent%2C%20ou%20par%20d%E2%80%99autre%20part%3B%20et%20celle%20que%20saut%20fuer%20par%20lai%20ou%20elle%20entre%2C%20c%E2%80%99est%20saiette%20entrans%20en%20leus%20charnus%2C%20et%20saut%20fuer%20aucune%20fois%20maintenant.)
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And if it does not jump now, let it be until the flesh is rotted around it, and the abscess is eased; and likewise if it is stuck in the bone, and it cannot come out, let it be like that for several days, and move it every day; and then it will jump, and if it does not jump, carefully cut around until all the tissue is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 And if the arrow is stuck in the skull bone, reaching one of the brain's ventricles, and any of the mentioned accidents happen to the patient: then do not pull it out, but let it be until it becomes even after several days, because if the arrow reaches the sylvian fissure, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow is not stuck only in the bone, and does not reach the marrow, and the patient remains for several days without any bad accidents, then attempt to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it is deeply stuck in this way and cannot come out, then apply a poultice around it, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And if the arrow is embedded in the body so that it cannot be seen, then search for it throughout the wound; and if you feel it, then pull it out with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound or the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then enlarge the wound until it is large; and pull the arrow out if you can, and if it has ears that hold it in place, then remove as much flesh attached to it as you can without breaking the arrow, and then bend or break the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrow so that you can pull it out more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	 And if you cannot do it at once, let it be until the place is swollen, then pull it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And if the bleeding caused by the decorremens (a type of injury) is contrary to this, moderate what we have said about the cure in its chapter; and be cautious of the incision of the nerve and vein, and use tricks to gently remove the arrow without danger, either quickly or slowly, firmly or carefully; and place the patient in the same condition that they were in when the arrow fell on them, for this is one of the greatest helps, and if you cannot do this, then place them as the signs show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 The arrow that comes from another direction, where something is visible on it, or the skin is swollen in a noticeable way: then cut there, as much as the pliers can reach, and then extract it; but be careful not to injure the patient further.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	 And if it is held in the bone, rotate your hand roundly, until it enters into the bone and expands the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 And if it cannot come out, leave it in and attempt extraction again until it comes out; and if a piece of the arrow remains, push the whole piece out; and if it has broken off, and you wish to administer a suppository, insert an appropriate instrument so that the tip of the arrow enters the hair of the instrument; then pull out, and if the arrow is stuck in there, insert the instrument with the tip entering first to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 And if the arrow is barbed, it is necessary to cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if possible, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And if the arrows fall in the foot or belly or bladder or ribs, and it is close by and can be covered, do so; and take care not to cover the vein and nerve, then extract it, and stitch the wound if necessary; and cure it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	 The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows resembles a bird's beak, and see the illustration here:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	 And there are many forms of them: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape of the arrowhead is like the feather of a bird, to attach to the tip of the arrow, such as this is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	 the shape of pliers for attaching and pulling out, such as this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	 of the common veins of the body.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 There are thirty-one veins in the body from which one can bleed, of which sixteen are: two that are behind the ears, called "herbech"; and the two arteries that are visible in the temples; and two veins that are in the armpts of the two eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is between the eyebrows; and the vein that is at the tip of the nose; and the two jugulars that are in the neck; and the two veins that are in the upper lips, which are called "augeherich"; and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins that are commonly bled are three in each arm: one is the cephalic, located on the left side, and called by laypeople "head vein"; the median is called "faste", and it is made up of the cephalic and basilic, and is called by laypeople "heart vein"; and the basilic is on the right side, and is called by laypeople "belly vein", and it is above the fascia, and it is the one that is apparent, manifestly visible on the arm.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And the "salvatelle" is the vein that is between the ring finger and the little finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is under the arch of the pocket on the left side, and the second is the saphenous which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein that is called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The bleeding of veins that are behind the ears helps against old catarrh and headaches;
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the temples is beneficial for chronic and sudden migraines, and customary eye inflammation, and watery eyes; and the qualities of the bleeding are as I tell you: and it is that the patient constricts their neck, so that the two veins appear clearly; and feel the pulse beneath your finger, and then stop it; then lift the skin above the vein up to your index finger, and insert the lancet underneath, and raise the vein up, and cut it, as you have done with the other veins, and let out the blood according to your need; then untie the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on it; and then bind it tightly, and leave it on until it heals; and we have already spoken of their binding and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 The bleeding of the frontal vein is worth as much as the bleeding of the cephalic in diseases of the face, and for migraines, and for redness; and its quality is such that the patient strains their neck by twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 And place the tip on the vein, and strike it with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you see; then loosen the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is healed and sometimes the work is done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	 Nevertheless, it is not appropriate for the flame to be too sharp and cutting, and to cut across, because the bone is close by, and there is a risk that the flame will break when it is fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 The incision of the two veins that are in the two temples helps the eyes, and the eyebrow, and the ringworm, and the inflammation in the eye, and diseases of the face; and the quality of their bleeding is such that the patient wrings their neck with some tie, as mentioned before; then the bleeding, whether it be through a wound or a little longer and wider, as there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	 And if the flame is fine, it may break; then make an incision in the vein, as much as you need, and then bind it with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The bleeding of the vein in the nose is beneficial for fever, and acute madness, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and inflammation that comes to the face, even when it is old; and the quality of the bleeding is such that the patient wrings their neck, then pulls their nose towards your left hand, and takes a fine, long flame, and sticks it between the upper lip in the space that is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open widely, and the blood will now begin to flow; and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your needs, then bind it for one night, for it is quickly restored; and this is the method of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The sap of two bindweeds helps with the tightening of the sinew, the beginning of paralysis, and many diseases, and impetigo, and corrosion, and herpes, and scabies; and the quality of the sap is such that the patient strains their neck below one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing over the patient's head, and the patient sit on a seat, then carefully open the vein wide, then draw blood gently, or as much as necessary; then perform the same procedure on the other vein, then untie the bandage, and moderately tighten both veins so that the patient does not choke; and let it be until morning, so that the wound dries.
de la sainie des leivres	 of the flow/discharge from the wounds/sores/ulcers
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	 The flow from the wounds/sores on the lips above assists in collecting in the mouth, and in the corruption of gums, cracking of lips, and nasal congestion and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the quality of the flow is such that it helps the patient sit in front of you, and hold their neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two wounds, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are recognized by being black, and by having small black veins around them: cut then both, and if you do not recognize them, and are in doubt, then cut the largest one on each side, and do the same for the two wounds that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 of saliva beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The saliva from veins that are beneath the tongue helps after the saliva of the head, and this is at the constriction of the throat, and in diseases of the eye, and in diseases of the mouth; and the quality of saliva is such that the patient lies down between your hands in front of the sun, and raises the tongue, and looks beneath on each side for a black vein: then heal both, but do not go too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The veins that are commonly bled are bled in two ways: either by pricking with a wide mirror-like flame, or with an olive-shaped subtle one like cutting tools, and it is called "anesil"; and they are large and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	 The shape of the myrtle flame is very famous, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 And it is necessary to use for opening veins that are full of thick, visible blood, and that contain clotted and turbid blood; and this is the shape of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	 and it is more finely pointed, and is used for healing delicate veins, where there is thin yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The healing of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are below the throat, and in the neck, chest, and abdomen; and it is necessary for the surgeon to heal by bleeding, while being careful not to touch the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And if he cuts the artery, and blood flows out, it must be stopped, as I have said; and the flame should not be piercing but cutting like a lancet.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the vein does not open manifestly, it should be constricted and replaced with another one; or you seek a branch of it, or you open a vein in its place in the arm: it opens manifestly; and cut it with a lancet-like flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you want to recognize the location of the venesection, it should be done thusly: you constrict the arm and feel for the pulse until you recognize the place; then mark the spot with ink and bind the arm; cut the vein with a lancet-like flame; and take care not to strike the artery when you see the swollen spot, for it is an arterial bleed: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you see it bulging up high, similar to a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is from the artery: hasten then, and place your hand on it for a long time, then remove your hand if the bleeding stops, which often happens; if the arm is swollen, leave it like that and do not move it, and let it be, and do not move it until it is healed; and beware, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	 And if the bleeding is not stopped and it overpowers you, and medicine is not present, cut the artery if it is visible, for its origin will retract; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 And take a bark of fennel, and split it, and take one half and bind it firmly until the next day; if the blood stops, it is good; if not, then treat it, as we have said, with powders that stop blood;
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The venesection in the middle helps in such a way that it drains blood from both above the head and below the body, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic, as we have said; and it is necessary for the surgeon to be cautious about the nerve that is underneath, and if it pricks too deep, and he finds the nerve, and it becomes inflamed and the wound becomes serious, and perhaps cannot be healed; and this nerve often appears, and if it does not appear in some men due to its delicateness, then you must cure it with a blunt instrument; and avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	 And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make an incision along it.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 The letting of blood from the cephalic vein is beneficial, for it draws blood from the head and helps the eyes; and one should bleed by pricking the olive-shaped or myrtle-shaped veins, for they are the safest of all veins, as there is no nerve or artery beneath them.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 Nevertheless, one should seek the least prominent location and not worry if one misses the first time, but instead try again; and it may be that the site becomes swollen for some men when they miss the first time, but this is of no concern.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	 The quality of the bleeding depends on your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing you should know about bloodletting is that it is not undertaken except to preserve health and avoid future illnesses; and let the bloodletting be done in one of the three veins, namely: the cephalic, basilic, or femorale; and one should let blood at the beginning of the day, in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and one should let blood on the first or third day, after two or three hours into the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 Bloodletting performed for illnesses does not have a predetermined time, but rather when necessary during the day or night, at all hours and in all times; and one should not let blood in children until they are 14 years old, nor in women carrying a fetus from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	 Do not at all attempt to heal the old who have passed sixty years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 And when anyone wishes to heal himself, in any way, he must first cleanse the intestines with a light enema if he has retained much feces, so that the veins do not draw out superfluidities from the intestines, harmful to the principal members; nor should one heal who is too full of food, or drunk, until they are sober, or dropsical; and one should not attempt to heal after colic passion, vomiting, diarrhea, frequent intercourse with women, work, staying up late, fasting, or any exhaustion, whether from a wound or the body; then thin out the humors if the blood is thick, through food and drink and medicines if you have them; then enter the bath if nothing prevents it, to thin out the blood, and heal the vein of the worst place around the third hour, as we have said; and be at rest that day from work, pain, lust, and similar things; and be happy and joyful, and let the healer wear a bandage higher than the patient's, and rub their arm two or three times, then loosen the binding in the middle, for when it is too tight or narrow, blood cannot flow; and then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell and become noticeable; then moisten the bandages with a little old oil, then place your left hand on the vein beneath the place you wish to heal, so that the vein does not move and fail when struck by the lancet.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 For there are veins that run like strings in the flesh, and some of them are full of airiness, such that when one applies fire, they contract and do not open, and thus it is with these; and if one opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore the surgeon must be aware in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	 And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; if not, try again a little below or above the same spot quickly, if the spot is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 And if the spot is swollen and the patient is frightened, leave it for a day or two and do not bind the arm: perhaps abscesses will form; do not enter the bath, then try again to open the vein if it pleases you; and if the opening is small, cut the skin carefully and you suspect that not enough blood will flow, then place the flame directly into the same hole; and perform the operation quickly, so that the spot becomes swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If you see the place swollen, do not restart the bleeding, and put a little bit of oil paste on it, for it clears the body from blood, and the oil is more effective in that place; and thus administer the oil paste in every bleeding that you stop the flow of blood; and this same mixture of oil and egg yolk, when applied to the swollen area, makes the vein shrink and spreads out when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if there comes a large abscess, which happens often, even when it is only bled at that time or the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put a wet sponge heated with water and a little salt on it, and hold it in place for an hour; and you should do this after the bleeding from the vein has stopped, and if some blackness or greenish color remains at the site after several days, it will not harm it; and if you wish, put something made of aloes or myrrh dissolved in sage juice on it.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	 And often there appears an abscess and discharge at the basis of the penis; place your hand therefore on it, and if you find a soft spot upon compression of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore be careful not to apply any of the things that we have mentioned, because perhaps you will injure an artery; but instead use a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	 And draw blood from each wound according to its quantity and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	 Because if the blood is black, let it flow until it turns red; and if it is thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.[important note: I am not a doctor and this translation does not constitute medical advice]
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And it is necessary for the person who is stout and strong, and in need of bloodletting, that they make a larger incision, and let the wound be wide; and for the one who is weak, do the contrary, and it is better to bleed them a little and frequently, and it should be bled by cutting across, not by stabbing; and this method of bleeding is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and is worth more than long or wide bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 And for the person whose body needs bleeding, it is necessary to give them a piece of bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if they are feverish, bleed them three or four times and if they have a cold complexion, feed them before the bleeding a piece of bread soaked in syrup made from mushed medlars, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and zedoary, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if he has a fever after the release of much blood, then it is necessary that he consume broth of meat, and fragrant subtle syrup, and make use of other things that we have said in the division or chapter of syncope, for the evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	 And if he wants to bleed his arm and purge himself again, then it is necessary, when he has been weakened by heavy bleeding, that he bleeds a little at a time, according to the amount of his remaining strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	 And whoever wants to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, let him bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.[Adding some contextual information: In medieval medicine, bloodletting (or phlebotomy) was a common medical practice used as a treatment for various symptoms and diseases. It was based on the theory of humoralism, where an imbalance in bodily fluids (known as "humors") could lead to illness. Bloodletting was believed to help restore balance by removing excess blood. The timing of bloodletting was important and depended on several factors such as the patient's strength and the stage of the disease.]
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	 And if one wants to heal from another part, they should do so on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 For there is much blood inside the body that is already heated and causes fever; therefore, one must draw out a large quantity and widen the opening until it reaches the desired size; then, after meeting all the conditions for healing, place your hand on their pulse as they heal, to prevent death from taking place of the healing process, which often happens when the healer is negligent; and it is not necessary to forcefully press down or suddenly extend the arm if blood must be released a second time and the opening has closed, but instead, leave it alone until it heals a second time; or apply the tip of a flame gently until the coagulated blood comes out of the vein, then place a piece of cloth soaked in water over it and press down lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	 And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not squeeze it, until the abscess has calmed down.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	 And if there is a need to draw blood again, do so in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	 The vein in the middle of the arm is bled instead of the vein in the head because it is composed (of more blood).
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the manner of bleeding is as follows: the patient puts his hand in warm water until the vein becomes visible and prominent; then it should be tied loosely so that the vein can be seen clearly, and bleed from it crossways, not too large or long; and make the incision wide, and bleed close to the joint of the hand, and if blood does not flow out, put the hand back in warm water and let the blood run into the water until you have enough; and if this is done in the summer, do not put the hand back in warm water, for it is more necessary to use it in winter than in summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than any other vein, as there are no arteries or nerves there.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 The sap of the salvation plant of the right hand is worthwhile for all liver diseases, and this is how it's done: straighten the hand, and place it in hot water until the vein rises, if one sees it; and if the sap flows sideways, and if you wipe it completely off, it doesn't matter; and don't go too deep, for the nerves are all stripped bare of flesh underneath, and then return the hand to hot water, if the blood is frozen in the wound, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	 And when you have drawn blood as much as is necessary, place oil and salt on the vein to quickly seal it, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	 The flow of sinus from him into the left hand is worthwhile for the disease of the scrofula, and does just as I have told you for the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The flow of pus from the armpit is beneficial for all diseases below the chest, such as diseases of the groin, swelling of the testicles, illness in the kidneys and thighs and legs, and similar ailments.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 And the quality of this flow is such that the patient should put their foot in hot water and rub it on the vein until it disappears, tying it above the ankle joint; and the vein runs along the ankle, going up the leg; so bleed at the largest vein, either at the ankle or above it, whichever is more convenient.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	 And if you heal it on the foot, watch out for the nerves that are underneath, and cut crosswise as in chopping; and let the flame be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	 And if the blood cannot come out, put the foot back in the water and let the vein empty completely.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 And if the sinew fails the first time, try again a little higher, for the place is salty; do not worry about nerves, as we have said, and do the same for the tendon of the other foot.[NOTE: I'm assuming "sainieres" and "sophene" both refer to some kind of tendon or sinew in this context, but I'm not certain.]
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	 The place of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the leg, and its incision is worth as much as the pain of a swelling, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 And the quality of his bleeding is such that the patient goes into a bath and strains above the ankle four times by twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, bleed him in all ways that you can, and crossing (veins); and it is better to cut rather than to cauterize, for the place is raw, and it is greatly susceptible to many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	 And if you do not find it (the bleeding point), bleed a few drops from it which will appear on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of nerves; and make the blood flow until you see it (the vein), then loosen the tie and put cotton on it and bind it; it is now bled.
des sainies de ventouse	 of blisters from cupping glasses
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	 Cupping glasses are made of horns, or of tin, or of glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And this cupping that is done without striking is also done in two ways: either with heat or without heat; and cupping that is done by striking and drawing blood is done in 14 places on the body, one of which is on the head; another is on the neck; two others are on both sides of the collarbone; a cup is placed under the chin; cups are placed on both shoulders; cups are placed on the loins; cups are placed between both arms; cups are placed on both legs; cups are placed on both ankles. This cupping does not draw blood, except for some small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken the body as one does when letting blood; and it should not be administered at all, neither with heat nor without heat, in any disease that comes from excess, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if by necessity of illness it is necessary to perform cupping, or for customary purposes, we administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at any time; for there are some who, when they need cupping, have a heavy head; and there are some who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkening of the eyes; and there are such ones who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and secrete blood; and there are those who dream, and see in their mind blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	 And when we see these signs, and similarly when it is in the middle of the month, we order them to be cupped after 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 The salve of the mouse helps with the cracking of the skull that comes to the eyes, and it should not be after the evacuation of the whole body; and this ventilation is in place of the salve of the head, and it should not be used by someone of a cold complexion or who has catarrh, for it does them great harm; and for this reason, old people should not use it, nor those who have cold diseases in their heads.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	 And those who use the salve frequently become forgetful, and therefore one should place the cup slightly lower with caution of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 The ventilation at the neck is in place of the salve of the head and basilisk, and therefore it is valuable for narrowing of the breast, and fissure of the channel of the nipple, and all ailments, and one must be careful to not apply it too firmly, for if it sticks too tightly, it may cause forgetfulness or stomach and heart repletion.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 The pains on the sides of the neck are as painful as headaches, and ophthalmia, and migraines, and strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is located near the basilic vein; and you should instruct the surgeon to be careful when making an incision, so as not to cut the artery, and cause a flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	 Swellings below the chin are as harmful as diseases of the mouth, and decay of the gums, and similar illnesses that occur in the mouth; and it is located near the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	 Swellings of the shoulders are as harmful as diseases caused by heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 Wounds of the thigh are as valuable as three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins; and it advises the surgeon not to strike too deep, for the place is bare of flesh, and there are nerves and arteries beneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	 The cupping glass on the buttocks is as valuable as hemorrhoids of the anus and diseases beneath; and it is necessary that the cupping glass be large and made of iron, for it needs to pull well; and perhaps if it were too fine, it would break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	 The cupping glasses on the legs heal openly, for they draw blood from all over the body, and are as valuable as ancient pains in the shins, and in the marrow, and in the bladder, and they cure boils; and they are placed on the inside of the two ankles, and on the two knees, but even so they weaken the body after long use, and cause paralysis in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	 The method for applying the cup is as follows: place it empty first, then apply it with steady suction, and do so quickly, while also moving it evenly. Do not stop doing this until you see the area become red and swollen, and notice the appearance of blood.
