Then pierce it, remove the cups, and pay attention to the condition of the body, for some have thin skin and visible veins: in such cases, pierce only once, and make wide and deep incisions; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	 And if the blood is thick, you should pierce twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	 And if the blood is very dense, you should pierce a third time; and when we want to draw out only a little bit of blood, we are satisfied with just one piercing.[](https://play.google.com/books/reader?id=9GkOAAAAYAAJ&hl=en&pg=GBS.PA17)
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if we want much blood, let us bleed frequently; and if the blood is thick, let us pierce deeply, and the endpoint is that the heart perceives it suddenly, and it is necessary for one who has tough and thick skin, and who have small pores, that you anoint the places of the cups with oil apertif and dissolutive: if it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of cucurbit seed; and if it is in winter, with oil of watercress, or lily, or chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	 And if the superfluities are abundant and cold, take oil of marjoram, or balsamite, or anise oil, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the one who is being treated has tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be put there, but it should be washed with water after ventosation (the action of introducing air into a cavity) of rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or gourd water, or porcelain water, or any similar thing.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	 And those who have a lot of moisture (in their body), let them rise from easel (a wooden support for holding a book or paper), or water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 And those who have coarse superfluities (excessive bodily fluids) rise from old wine, or water of vinegar, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or similar things; and one should not be bled with a cupping glass (a small cup used to create a vacuum on the skin for therapeutic purposes) before bathing or in the bath, but after the bath one hour or two; and they must not sleep after being cupped, and it is necessary that they stay awake, both when they are about to be cupped and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And beware if the one who is healing is coleric, and if the blood is too thick and inflamed; so they must take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces at ease, and similar things; and eat poultry, and meat of mutton, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And those who have a cold complexion should take honey syrup, and scented middle-aged wine, which is between old and new, and eat poultry, and small birds and squabs; and on the day that they will be evacuated, they should drink more than they eat; and it is appropriate to give some people triacle or muscatel before or after the evacuation, to comfort the principal members; and let the blood be thinned, but it is not suitable for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 Cupping glasses that are placed without causing harm are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, gout, stomach, belly, groin, and legs, because these members do not tolerate being struck. And one does not do this except to draw blood from member to member, as we place on the breasts when the milk is flowing. To remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place cups on the stomach and on the belly to reduce the size of the member. And it removes pain when there is an abscess or stone, and perhaps by its attractive power it draws out the abscess, or dissolves the stone from its place. And it does this when one places it on the liver and on the spleen when there is trapped wind. These cups are administered empty to only suction. And sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes full of warm water, as in cases of pleurisy. And in such a way that one fills the cup with hot water, or water in which suitable herbs for this have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	 The shape of the cupping device used with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it should be 2 fingers wide and half a palm deep, and have a small hole on the side near the middle for inserting a needle, and it should be made of brass, smooth beforehand so as not to wound the patient when placing it on the body part; and in the middle there should be an iron or steel crossbar for holding a lit candle, and they should come in various sizes according to the illnesses and ages of those who use them; for the cupping devices used on children are different than those used on adults, and those used on thin people are different than those used on fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And one should apply the cupping device to the body part in this way: light the candle made of wax or linen and insert it through the crossbar inside the cupping device, positioning it so that the flame is at the bottom of the device and does not burn the patient; then place the cupping device on the body part, with your fingers covering the hole we mentioned earlier, in order to create a vacuum when you are ready; remove the cupping device and repeat the process as needed by re-lighting the candle and placing it back inside the crossbar.[
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the cupping glass then, which is administered in cases of pleurisy, it has no rod or opening, and is only applied when it is full of water, and is placed solely on the body; and this is its method:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Splinters are only applied to small areas where cupping glasses cannot be placed, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and on bare surfaces like the palm or nose, and others similar; and the quality of the splinter is such that when you find splinters that are in clean, clear water without putrefaction, take them; and place them in a nut filled with clean water until they become tame and have nothing left in their bellies; and then let it be bled and cupped, then rub the body part until it becomes red, and place the splinters on top; and when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where a cupping glass can be placed, do so, for it is very beneficial.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If not, lift the armpit and then the chest, very gently, and then compress; and if the swelling takes too long to recede after the body, wet a linen cloth in cold water and place it on until the swelling subsides; and if the swelling is multiplied, put crushed vitriol, or aloes, and similar things on it until it subsides; or you put half of peeled beans on the affected area and leave them until they dry at the spot, this will stop it now; and if you need more, take other lymph nodes.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And if the lymph nodes do not want to swell, rub the area with fresh blood or insert a needle until the blood comes out, then put them on and as soon as they feel the blood, they will dry; and when you see that they are falling off, dust a little bit of crushed aloe and salt, or ash, on it and they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	 Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	 This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and deals with the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Know, dear son, that foolish surgeons throw aside this chapter, as they have never seen any of the ancient books nor read a letter; and for this reason, knowledge is strange in our land, for I never found any good one; and I know nothing about it, except through the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated its science, and by experience, and by the habit of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what it contains, and summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are prepared, as I did in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	 It is thus appropriate that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the content and the chapters where the wise man directs his understanding, and remains true to it, so that those who have been tested may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 I say that when fracture or dislocation or twisting or crushing happens to anyone, you should quickly heal the patient from one side and the other, if no obstacle prevents it, such as weakness of the body, infants, the elderly; or if the time is not extremely hot, or too cold; and eat dry foods, that is, cool games, and bird and hare meat, and do not drink wine, nor eat fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you are free from fear of a hot abscess, or spreading matter to the limb; so that the patient returns to their usual regimen.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	 And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that promote solid thickening, such as wheat cooked in water, and bread, meat, cheese, and dairy products, and eggs, and fresh fish, and robust wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	 For with suitable nourishment, movement returns and fractures heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that the broken bones of the old and infirm cannot heal or knit together well according to their nature due to the weakness of their bodies, nor can those who are too young, such as the bones of small children; but it doesn't matter, reset the broken bone and use strong ligatures to hold the member together until it heals as it was before; and do not interfere with its healing process, and therefore it must be nourished with hearty foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	 And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	 For a break of the skull is different from a break of the hip or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	 For there are some fractures that go along the grain, and others that split, like the shaft of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	 And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with only a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And each type has its own method and proper instrument for restoration, according to what the symptoms suggest; and a fracture of the bone is recognized by its being twisted and clearly visible, and producing a sound when pressed with the hand; but if there is no twisting or sound, and the patient does not feel great pain, then it is not a fracture; however, there may be twisting, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	 You should not move it with your hand, but apply the following medications and then gently bind it.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that for the fracture in a branch, where the two parts are disjointed, they should now be aligned equally, so that pus does not develop; and if pus forms, then leave it alone for a day until it subsides; then align it as easily and securely as you can, and know that the restoration of this is easier than one where pieces are involved; then bind it as described hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And if the bone is shattered into pieces, stretch it from two sides whether it is an arm or a leg, or with your hand if it is a small member, or with two ropes, or with one rope and your hand; and place the member in its natural position so that when the broken parts of the member are separated, you bring them together in their places as easily and securely as you can, and ensure that your work does not cause harm or pain to the patient; and align the two ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	 And he can feel it with his hand if it does not seem to be well: so straighten it nicely, and do not strain it too much, nor press as those who bring about a hot and constricted abscess in the member through their work, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limb is healed, chastise the patient so that they do not move it, whether awake or asleep, turning or in any other way; and make sure that the limb is secured so that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 For when it feels any pain, it is not healed, and it must be put in such a position that it feels no pain; and make sure that it is set straight, so that there is no crookedness when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken member are as I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	 Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and in size and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 Know that there are small members, such as arms and legs and the like: these should be wrapped in soft and fine linen bandages; and those that are large, such as hips and legs: these should be wrapped in a wide and firm binding, for a wide binding embraces the entire limb and constricts it equally on all sides, so that there is no swelling; then wrap light sponges around it, three or four times according to the limb, and lightly press your hand over the entire binding; then go above the fracture and press less, so that the fracture moves away a little; and gradually loosen the binding until you encompass a large part of the healthy limb, then take another binding and wrap around again on the broken limb; then return to the area below the fracture, and constrict it moderately, not too tight or too loose, as we have said in the first passage above; then place linen or cloth stuffing between the bindings, so that they are all even, then tie everything with a bandage on top, and then place well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 And if there is swelling or abscess, place something warm and soothing for an abscess on it, and that which reduces swelling, and leave it in place for several days; then pull tight on your stirrups, and let the bleeding be half the width of a reed, or from a stick that is used to make roof tiles, or from palm branches, and let them be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 But it is necessary that the stirrup placed on the fracture be slightly larger and wider than the others; and be also as long as is needed for the size or length of the limb; then pull tight on your stirrups as you did at the first juncture, then bind a suitable thread over it, as was done at the first juncture on the fracture; tighter is better, less so; and it is necessary that the thread be of medium thickness, not too thick or too thin, and be made of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of foolish people who bind their wounds with twisted string from a loom, this is a great error, for the binding cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it is not at all appropriate to have less than two finger-widths of space between each stirrup.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	 And if the patient is wounded by the shards of arrows after being pulled out in healthy places, place under them lint or wool padding, so that they do not cause further injury.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	 When the wound is accompanied by a fracture and the bones are broken, I will tell you the cure following this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	 And know that it is not appropriate to pull out all fractured arrow(s) on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 Because when the limb is large, it is not appropriate to insert arrows(s) before 5 or 7 days, or more depending on your certainty of a hot abscess occurring; and here follows the method of ancient poultices for healing fractures, dislocations, and twisting: take some flour that holds to the mill walls, mix it with plenty of egg, and apply this concoction, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it. And this is the common method of the poultice that restores fractures in many ways, and also for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	 Another manner of plaster restores breaks and dislocations and distortions: take three [units of] aloeswood and ladanum and electampane and asafetida and gum arabic and myrobalans, in the quantity of ten units; myrrh and aloes, in the quantity of five units; alechoil nine units; and grind into a powder, and mix with egg white; if the complexion of the person is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another manner of plaster that is beneficial for distortions: take myrobalans and coltsfoot, in the quantity of ten units; myrrh and aloes, in the quantity of nine units; frankincense six units; bdellium Armeniacum ten units, and grind well, and make into a paste with water or egg white, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another way of emplaster for joints and separated bones in their places, and to appease the resulting pain, and for the cure of fractures and breaks: take new wool, and soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and put it on the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This emplaster does not restore [the limb], but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	 Another way of emplaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and crushed broad-leaved plantain leaves, grind them together, and make an emplaster.[*Plantago major is commonly referred to as "broad-leaved plantain"]
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another way of emplaster for the restoration of bone fractures and to soften the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take root of wormwood, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of peas, of each one part; and grind, and make into a paste with wine, and if the limbs are heated, mix it with moist coriander water, or with water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another way of making a more powerful plaster than the first, when a hard abscess comes to restore the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take roots of wormwood, and seeds of flax, balm, melilot, and elder, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all of them one part; and grind, and make into a paste with brine water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	 Hippocrates says in his book that one should not place anything on the broken limb to restore it, except for a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be moderate, neither too hard nor too soft.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	 And it seems that Galen thinks that one should place dry, slightly warm things on the broken limb to restore it, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	 Another type of plaster that is effective for wounds and pain: take the genitals and chopped-off hair of a decapitated man, or bird feathers, and wormwood, and also salt, and grind them, and make a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then wait a bit and make sure the patient feels no pain, and that the bones have not moved from their place; and do not unlock it for many days. And if pain comes to the area, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry and unlock it, and remove the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and a sea sponge soaked in water, and raise the area, until the itching stops, and the pain is calmed; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry wool, dampened with water or rose oil, and bind it tightly to ensure there is no inflammation; and let the inflammation of the member subside, and the pain be removed, then begin the binding again gently, and a little plaster, and do not tie it as tight as before; and bind it gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	 And if you see that an abscess with redness, pain, and swelling has healed completely, and you need to apply a plaster and bandage, then reapply it as you did before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 And if no improvement comes to the limb from what we have said, do not unbind it until after three days, or four, or five, or seven; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, depending on what one sees, so that the swelling can subside, and bring the limb closer to the flesh; then bind it more tightly than before, and let the flesh grow back as I mentioned earlier; and if you see the joint drying out more than necessary, know that no pus can come there; therefore anoint it with warm water each time you unbind it, every third day, and loosen the binding a little; by this work, the pus will subside in the limb, and quickly heal what foolish surgeons do, who restore the limb out of place: that is bad, and such work is dangerous, and I see no other option but to rest and work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	 of the different ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 There are many ways of fractures, and various shapes, and the causes are distinct; for there are fractures made by sword blows, and the neck takes out all the bone down to the syphac which is beneath the bone, as a hatchet or stick does; and this kind of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	 When the sword cuts the bone from above without penetrating it, and this kind of fracture is called "absolue"; and the wound of these two fractures can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	 And if there is an embedded blow, or splitting, or from a stone club, or falling on a stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	 And if it has a fracture reaching up to the membrane that is beneath the bone, or above it, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if there is a wound that is sunken into the bone as thin as a hair, and the fracture is small, and this type of fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound is made by striking a stone, or falling, or by some similar thing, and causes a piece of the bone to sink inward, and the place is rough like when a blacksmith hammers on cauldrons; then stones enter inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And this happens more frequently in those who have moist bones in their head, such as in children; and this occurs in all types of fractures where small pieces are separated like this; and I will speak about that later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	 And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the withdrawal (traction) on them, and through examination by probing, and by the corrupt flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	 A hairline fracture is recognized by this: when the bone is exposed and one rubs over it, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	 In the treatment of a fracture, be aware of the patient's condition, and if you see any adverse symptoms, such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, trembling, ague fever, eyes turning out and reddening, and other similar symptoms in various dispositions, then it cannot heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	 And if you do not see frightful symptoms and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	 And when the wounded person first comes to you, and it's in winter, then you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the latest when you are able to.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	 And if it is in the summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone does not become corrupt and the complications that we have mentioned do not occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 And if the fracture of the bone reaches the tissue that covers the brain, then you should cut open the injured part in this way: take hold of the patient's head and expose the bone as much as you can, in a manner suitable to the wound, and gently expose the wound. If blood flows out when the bone is exposed or if there is an abscess, provide the necessary aid. Then fill the opening with cloths soaked in rose oil and let the wound rest until the abscess has healed and you are sure that there is no more bleeding. After that, begin to remove the bone, which can be done in two ways: one way is to make a narrow incision in front, and this is the method:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	 And then put in another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	 And the second manner is that you have a number of different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of iron; and work lightly, so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	 And if the bone is hard and protruding, you must bore around it so that you administer cuts with trepan drills, not too deep that they do not penetrate beyond the skull, and there should be above the tip a margin or circle that does not allow the tip to go beyond the bone; and you must have several, so that each one comes in its place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have trepan drills for all parts of the skull; and this is the shape of the three types of trepan drills.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	 The qualities for drilling around the broken bone are: place a drill on the bone, and turn it towards your hands until you know the bone is pierced; then move the drill a little further and do the same all around, then cut along the incisions the width of the bone that is between the holes, and do this as delicately and lightly as you can, as we have said, so that you draw out the bone with your hand or with one of the tools you have such as tongs, pincers; and make sure you do not touch the brain or the membrane.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, it is necessary to blunt the sharpness that remains from the bone on all other similar tools like an incisor, but it should be more slender and fine than the other incisors; and if there remain any small bones or scales, remove them lightly with the tools; then cure the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	 And the other manner of work is that which Galen describes, which is safer; and he praises it greatly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	 First, you must expose a part of the bone where the break is clearly visible. Once you have exposed that part, place the rounded head of this scalpel underneath it, like so:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 And do not cut all the way through from one side, but rather make an incision along the bone on both sides, with the edge of the scalpel facing towards the bone. Then gently tap on the small mallet to fracture the bone completely around, taking great care not to damage the tissue beneath. It can be easily removed without harm or fear.[English text translation by User]
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	 And if the break of the bone does not pierce through to the outer layer, and the bone is only cut through at the top, with small pieces, then you must smooth over that roughness, and remove the splinters with a sharp razor which you should have in various quantities, to make suitable adjustments in each place, according to the task and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	 First, use great razors, and then smaller ones, and do not stop doing so until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	 In each other fine cutting of hair and delicate break, you must adjust according to its alignment; this is not an easy matter for one who has devoted their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 And if the abscess is uncovered, take a linen cloth of appropriate size for the wound, wet it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another double-layered cloth and wet it with wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth; do this as gently as you can so as not to harm the abscess, then apply another ligament over it without tightening it too much, just enough to hold the wound together; leave it like that for a day or two until the abscess has calmed down, then remove it and apply medicines such as lily roots, vetch flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; make a powder out of these and put it on the wound, and continue to apply painless medicine; ensure that the wound stays clean, that there is no residue or accumulation of pus, because when pus collects under the cloth covering the brain, it will rot and cause great harm to the patient; for when something sharp is placed on the abscess, it causes further damage.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	 Take heed, if any misfortune befalls the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful in doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if no pus comes out except for what was put there by the medicine, and it has such power, then you should take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and soak a cloth in it, and place it on the styptic; then cure it in various ways as necessary, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	 Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one part by itself, because they are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, but only swells or becomes twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should insert your little finger or the tip of the nose and align the break with your index finger on one side and your thumb on the other, until the nose regains its natural shape; do this gently and make sure that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	 And if the fracture is above the nael, and the swelling cannot come to the place, then you should align it even with the head of a thick rod.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 And if the fracture is in two parts, then do likewise (align it), and hurry to set it on the first day if you can; if not, after the seventh or the tenth day, when the abscess has subsided, then bind a bandage of linen cloths to the head of the nael if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	 Or you should put one (bandage) on one side and the other on the other side if the fracture is there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the nael's openings.[Safe Browsing]{"action":"del","message":"Warning: Some potentially dangerous content has been detected. Proceed with caution."}
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And said some physician that one should moisten the bandages with butter, and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 It does not seem good to me, but it is necessary that they are moistened with a mixture of egg yolk and powdered flour; then leave the bandage until the bone is healed and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	 And sometimes goose feathers are put in place of bandages, and gently wrapped with a soft cloth, and the healer holds it in place while the patient blows through it; do as you please.[(Note: This translation is based on the assumption that "briseure" refers to the person holding the feather in place. However, another possible interpretation of this passage could be "and the breaker (or fractured bone) heals itself", if "briseure" is taken as a noun referring to the fracture.]
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	 And if pustules or boils come upon the nose while you are working, put on it cerote (a type of salve or plaster) or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a paste of diachylon (a type of adhesive plaster).
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if pustules or boils do not come, put an emplaster (medicated paste) on the outside, made of wild celery flour, and powdered incense, congealed with egg white; then apply light wool compresses, but do not bind it too tightly. If the break in the nose is small and it is broken into small pieces, extract them with appropriate instruments, then stitch the wound, and cure any foreign matter or dead flesh with suitable emplasters and ointments. And if there is no wound inside the nose, cure it with bandages and put sticks of wood inside until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	 of the dislocation of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	 When the jaw is dislocated below, and there is no wound on the outside, and only the joint is affected without being broken in two, except for some cartilage inside, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	 If the break is on the right side, you should put your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the break is on the left side, insert your index finger of the right hand, and gently push the break back into place, and adjust it with the other hand from the outside, and align it.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	 And if the break of the jaw is separated into two parts, you should apply extension to both parts until they are aligned.[Notes: The word "aministres" in Old French means "to provide or administer". Here, it has been translated as "apply" to convey the idea of applying an action or treatment. Also, the phrase "extension de II pars" refers to extending or pulling apart both parts of the broken jaw to align them correctly.]
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	 And if movements of the teeth occur, or a fracture, then bind them with a gold or silver or silk thread, then place a piece of clay on the broken jawbone, and place on it a double cloth; and place on the cloth a large star well made, or a piece of leather of equal size, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it to the chin as tightly as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and give them light meals.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	 And if you see that the shape changes, then loosen it on the third day, and then reset what has shifted; and apply a plaster to it, made of powder from the mill with plenty of egg or chickpea flour, after removing the clay; and place light linen on the plaster, and if the plaster dries out, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it heals; often it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	 And if abscesses become worse, soothe (ease) as we have often said.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	 And if there is a fracture and wound together, see if any piece of the bone has been removed; remove it so delicately with appropriate instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	 And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when you have removed all those pieces, and there is none left, then stitch the wound if it is wide, and apply appropriate plasters to it for promoting flesh growth until it is healed.[/Note: The word "emplaustres" refers to a type of medical plaster that was used in medieval times. It could be made from various substances such as herbs, resins, or waxes, and was applied to wounds or sores to promote healing and prevent infection.]
de la forcele	 of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	 The forceps breaks frequently in front, toward the shoulder, and the breakage is in three ways: either it is broken and separated into two pieces, which is easier to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	 And the procedure is as follows when the breakage is without a wound: that you have two assistants, one of whom holds the part with the broken forceps; and the other extends the neck toward the side; then place the break between your hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor gap.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And if you need to extend further, place a round cushion of cloth or wool under the patient's shoulder blade, and extend and lift the forceps, and press down on the cushion with your hand, so that you can place the break correctly
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	 And if you cannot pull the head of the humerus outward, because it is too far in, then the patient should lie on his other shoulder, place a middle pillow under the shoulder, and have the assistant push the shoulder downward, until the bone of the humerus is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	 And then align the fracture with your hands, and if you find it shattered, then you should saw across; gently pull out the pieces, and if the bones cannot join due to any obstruction, then use one of the incisions you made; but place this instrument, the syfac, beneath the humerus to protect it.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 and looks like a spoon, but is not sharpened, and should be as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and it should have two edges, one wide and one narrow, similar to the edge of the wound you made when you pulled the bones; and when you are certain that there is no hot abscess, then stitch the wound, and if the opening is small, or if you suspect a hot abscess, then pack the wound with lint and bandages, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	 And if abscesses appear, wet a towel in rose oil, vinegar, and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 The binding of the bone, when it is without wounds and without a surgeon, is to place poultice of molin powder and egg white on the bone, and put light wadding on top, and place a sphere underneath if needed; then take a very large bandage one palm wide, then put a double towel on the wadding and poultice; then take a subtle strap three digits wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the ends hang down; and place the strap on the break, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the healthy and injured shoulder blade; and bind each part, and when you see that the binding holds the break well, and you clearly see that the strap does not move above the bone, then rebind it every day, and when the ligature loosens, tighten it again; and make the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow under the shoulder blade when he sleeps, to lift the shoulder in elevation; this relieves the force of the break by aligning the shoulder, where you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless bad accidents occur, for up to 20 days; then reapply the poultice if needed, and bind and leave it like that until healed; and it is usually healed within 28 days, and in less time for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	 of the shoulder dislocation
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 It rarely happens that the shoulder breaks or dislocates in such a way that it is visible from the outside, and one can only detect it through touch; one should arrange it according to the pattern of the break, and reset it according to its natural shape, in every possible way; then put powder of flour with plenty of egg white, and light bandages, and place a double cloth on top; then place a wide and thin board over it, slightly larger than the shoulder, and if there are any hairs under the board from any part of the shoulder, one should fill those areas with linen bandages, so that the board rests evenly; and then bind it tightly with a large bandage, making sure the board does not move from its place, and check the binding every day; and whenever it loosens, tighten it, and make sure the board is in its place, and have the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 or 25 days. And when this number of days is completed, one should unbind it, and be careful, for it is not an easy thing for a bone to come out of place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	 And if a piece of the bone juts out in front, but not beneath the skin, then make an incision, and remove it, and do what we have said in the breaking of the forearm to soothe the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	 In the breaking of the hip.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 The thigh is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 And when it is broken in the middle, it droops downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of appetite, and perhaps vomits blood, and the fracture can be seen in the broken bone, and one can clearly tell.[](Note: I corrected "li chevemens" to "la chevauchement", which means "the fracture")
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the restoration is that the patient lies down on his back, and place a cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and bring the ribs from the two sides to your hands, and subtly make it even in every way that you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then apply poultices and compresses on top of the fracture, thin and salty, or made of light wood, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it to the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the bandage around to the back, and tighten it appropriately, and check every hour if it has softened, and if it has, then tighten it; and if it needs to be loosened, because of corruption or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and loosen it, and remove the poultice, and treat what has come there with methods of cures; then remoisten the poultice, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	 of the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	 Know that the breaking of ribs does not come about except in heavy blows to the back, and at the chest within, and they do not bend except because they are slippery; and one can feel it well upon examination at the sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the setting of the break is such that you place the fracture evenly, as is proper.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 And then apply the poultice and bind it with a splint if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	 And if the breaking of ribs is displaced inward, then the patient feels great pain and shortness of breath, as with pleurisy, because the bone punctures the lining; and breathing is difficult, and he quickly vomits blood, and this indicates serious illness; and the ancients have applied much skill to it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	 And there are some who say that one should administer foods that inflate the belly, to drive out the obstruction.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	 We do not do this, as it will cause abscesses to form if they have not already, if it is done.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	 And if they have already formed, then cleanse them.[translation request for the next sentence would be appreciated!]
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	 And some of you have said that cupping should be applied to the area to strongly draw out impurities, and this seems reasonable. However, there is a risk that the cups will attract impurities to the area due to its weakened state.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	 And some of you have said that the area should be covered with a wool cloth soaked in warm oil and bandages should be placed between the ribs to evenly apply pressure around it, then treated with the treatment for pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot endure by the bone pointing through the skin, and the patient is fearful, then a cut should be made above the broken rib, and an instrument placed underneath to protect the lung; and then the bone should be cut and gently removed, and then the two edges of the wound sewn up, if they are large, and treated with poultices, until it has healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if an abscess should arise, place dampened cloths with rose oil on it, and place it on the affected area; treat the area as needed for the abscess, and lie down on your side next to where it is, until it has healed.
de la brisure dou col	 of the break (fracture) of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	 Never does a break occur in the bones of the neck, and it rarely happens that it bends; and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will recover or not, observe whether you see their hands weakened, swollen, and discolored, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you poke them with a needle, they do not feel it.[
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that it is mortal in many ways (i.e., there are many factors that make the situation deadly), and if they move and feel when they are squeezed and poked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if proper treatment is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And if such a thing comes to the spine of the back, and you wish to know if it will be healed or not, look to see if the feet are weak, and if there are symptoms in the hands, and on the back an uncontrolled blowing and purging; and when it has been lain on its belly, there is an uncontrolled purging.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And when it is laid on its back and it wishes to turn over, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Know that it is mortal: it will not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	 And if these symptoms do not come to it, the matter is easier.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.
