And the treatment is that you search for whether there is a hot abscess, then place rose oil or egg yolk oil on the spine until it is calmed; then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters and bind it with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and let him not sleep on the part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And if any bone gets dislocated, it is necessary to cover it with a bandage; and remove the bone, then stitch the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then cure it with a healing ointment, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "head of the cow", insert your left hand pocket, and align it with your other hand to your ability, then apply the poultice and bandage if necessary; then bind it, and if there is a dislocated bone, do it again, and remove it, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	 of the fracture of the shin bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	 Not often does the shinbone get broken, and if it does happen, only a little shrinkage at the top occurs; and it becomes long, and bends to the side, and comes to the patient pain in the area, and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	 And the restoration is as follows: you extend your hand over it, up to the break; and you should know the shape and form of the break; and if the break is only at the top, then make the broken ends even, so that it returns to its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	 And if the break is long or it bends inward, then make the patient lie on their stomach, so that the restoration of the break becomes clear to you.[](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dQw4w9WgXcQ)
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	 And when you have set it evenly, apply the poultice, then place a stick or splint on it, and hold the break in place so that it does not move; and apply the bandage below the ribs, until the binding is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	 And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	 And if abscesses come to a head, do not touch them until the abscess has calmed down, and apply what we have previously mentioned; then return to the treatment, holding it in place as is necessary, unless there is an adverse event; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	 of the dislocation of the shoulder.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	 The shoulders are the part between the neck and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored in one of two ways: the first is to take a rod of medium size, according to this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	 And bind the two parts of the shoulder with two bands and pull them up, and have the patient sit on a chair; then lay his broken arm over the rod, so that it reaches the armpit and forms a curve around the wood, then place it under some heavy object or have the assistant stretch it downward; then align the broken ends in the hands of the surgeon, until the break returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	 And the other manner is to position the patient on his back, and tie his hand to his neck, then command two assistants to hold what is above the break with their hands, and the other holds below all the sinews, and each extends it in its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 And if you wish the extraction to be stronger, then tighten the sinew below the break and above the break, and each of the assistants extends it in its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the break is near the shoulder joint, then you must put one sinew in the middle beneath the armpit and another sinew lightly, without force, so that the break is aligned with the place and the shoulder; then align the break as it should be and tighten it, unless abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	 And if abscesses come to a head, do not bind it immediately for seven days, and place damp linen soaked in rose oil on it, until the abscess has subsided; then bind it, and the method of binding is such that you apply the poultice on the armpit, then place the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or chest; and place the cloth, and bind on the armpit, and on the arm, so that the arm remains in a stable position, unless something prevents it, or if the bones are not broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	 And if you are unsure whether the bones are broken, use splints, and place a wider and stronger splint on the fracture than the others, with a space of one span between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it extends beyond the fracture by three digits on either side; then bind on the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the fracture, more tightly and less when moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 And if you see the swelling and tightening, as we have said, at the time you restore the broken member, and you doubt a hot abscess, then let it be bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at the binding every three days to see if itching, inflammation, or discharge comes to the place, or if circulation cannot reach the member because the binding is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If it heals, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 And if no such accidents occur, then do not unbind it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach; and place a cushion filled with evenly distributed wool beneath the shoulder, and check every hour of the day or night to see that the shape of the broken member does not change or that the binding has not loosened; then heal it by the power of medicine, and give them the food that we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is at first subtle; and when they begin to recover, let the food be thicker.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 And it is customary for the shoulder and leg to be reset within forty days; and then one should release it and administer baths and medicinal ointments to straighten the limb.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the stricture is severe and embedded, one should wait to release it for ten days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	 of the arm fracture
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	 The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile", one of which is small and is the one that follows the armpit; and the other is large and is the one that is beneath, towards the little finger; perhaps the large foscile breaks alone, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 When the small bones are broken, the restoration is easy, and so is the healing; and when the large ones are broken, the healing is difficult, and more severe than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If only the small bone is broken, then it should be lightly stretched and aligned properly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 And if it is the large bone that is broken, then it must be squeezed more forcefully and stretched on a cushion. The patient's hand should be raised higher than the other one, and the little finger lower than the others. The patient should be crosswise on top of it, with the cushion raised higher in front of them so that they do not experience any discomfort. Then, the assistant should extend the patient's arm below the injured area towards their hand or to the ligament, and another assistant should do the same above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 And then the physician places it evenly, in the best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	 And if in the fracture there are pieces, place each one in its proper position, and if any piece is separated and pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its proper position, saw through and remove the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	 And if there is a wound with the fracture, I have spoken of this in a previous chapter; so treat it accordingly.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 And if inflamed abscesses occur at the beginning of the restoration, take a piece of cloth dipped in a mixture of oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and apply it gently on top until the abscesses have subsided.[References to "chaus" might refer to abscesses or other inflamed areas. The word "restorement" likely refers to an attempt at setting a fracture or reducing a dislocation.]
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 And then remove the cerote, and apply the plaster of powder from the mill with plenty of egg, then put on the bandages, and let the bandage of the breaker be stronger, and a little larger than the others; and know that it should have six bandages or arms in multiple dispositions: either the breaker is in one of the bones, or in two; and tighten more above the breaker than any other place, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are on the breaker be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread, with which it is tightened, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And reward the member and the ligament after several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And if any bad accidents happen to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then you should moisturize the member with warm water until the itching is calmed down; and let the member not be tightly restricted.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 And then resume tightening, and if the ligament is weakened and the bones dislocated, and similar things, address them.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	 And take note if the circulation cannot reach the member because it is too tight, then you should loosen it slightly and leave it like that for several days, until the circulation returns, and then you can tighten it again.[Note: I am not a medical professional, and this translation should not be used as medical advice. Please consult with a healthcare provider if you have any medical concerns.]
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of the things we have mentioned come to the patient, then do not release it for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 And apply a bandage around, then place their hands on their neck, making sure their collars are even, and be cautious of movement and chafing, and have them sleep on their backs; and know that this broken bone will be healed in 30 days or 35, and perhaps even in 20 days, depending on the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	 about the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	 Know that breaks in the back of the hand and at the knuckles of the fingers often happen, and they rarely come but rather bend many times.[](Note: I interpreted "ploieure" as a typo of "pluseurs", which means "many" or "several".)
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	 And when the fingers of the hand are broken or bent, then the patient should sit cross-legged, and sit directly in front of them equally; then place his hand on a stretched out cloth, and straighten the broken bones, and align them properly, so that they are well joined; and apply the poultice and bandages, if pus does not come, then place a stick according to the size of the place; and it should be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	 And if the break is on the outside around the belly of the hand, then make a ball of cloth, and instruct the patient to squeeze it to his broken hand; and then bind it with a long piece of cloth, and let the stick be as soft as the palm of the hand, and bind it as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	 And if the fracture is protruding, you should place a stick on top, and another below in the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind the whole hand, and tighten the binding between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	 And if the fracture comes to any of the fingers, if it's the thumb, set it evenly as it should be; and bind it with the palm, and if you see fit, place a small straight stick to raise the fracture and keep it from moving; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, set it evenly and bind it with the healthy finger that follows; or bind them all together, whichever is best, or place a stick on top, as with the thumb; and be attentive to the restoration and positioning of hot abscesses, and care for those who come there, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	 of the broken thigh/hip joint
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	 The thigh bone is often broken and it is clearly visible when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration consists of tying a ligature above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	 And the patient lies on their back, then each assistant extends their ligature to their respective equal parts; and this is when the break is between the bones.[Notes: Here "minister" or "ministres" (masculine form) refers to assistants or helpers who are aiding in the medical procedure. The word "faice" here likely refers to the patient's face or the front part of their body, as they are instructed to lie on their back.]
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the break is close to the root of the thigh, then let one of the ligatures be towards the groin, and the other ligature below the break.[Notes: Here "racine" refers to the root or top part of the thigh bone (femur) near the hip joint. The word "poignil" likely refers to the inguinal region or the area around the groin where the femoral artery and vein are located.]
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And if it is close to the knee, let the bandage be below the knee, and let there be extension downwards; then let the surgeon place the bone evenly with his two hands, until it is in its natural shape, and then apply the poultice and bind it, if pus does not appear.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	 And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside and then return to your work and care; the binding is done in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 It is necessary that you wrap around the broken bone with a bandage doubled in two or three layers, leaving the excess hanging; then bend the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and place a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, with the ends coming up; then bend back over the leg and thigh the bandage, then place a splint on the broken bone; then apply soft rags dipped in liquid between the leg and the thigh to ensure equal tension, then begin to bind firmly three or four times around the splint; and as you go higher above the splint, bind less tightly; then attend to the two ends of the thread that you placed between the leg and the thigh, and tie three knots in them that are above, then return down to the head of the thread until you come to the foot; and bind it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, as long as no abscess, swelling or other such thing appears.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	 And if it happens, loosen it, and adjust what comes out, as we have said many times; and if there are fragments of the bone that prick, they must be removed if possible; and if not, the place must be broken and opened; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	 And sometimes the hip is broken so that steel pins are put in, as in the shoulder and the arm; yet, in such a restoration, the patient does not fare well.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	 And know that the hip is restored in L days, or a few more or less, depending on the diversity of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	 of the groin of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the hollow of the knee often occurs a slight break, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 And if it breaks, it is only a split or hole, and this happens with all wounds, open or not, and it is easily felt.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the restoration is to place evenly what has been dislocated at its joints until it can move again; then apply the ointment and place a round bandage if necessary. Then bind it appropriately, and take care of all other considerations for breaks as we have said in other instances, such as hot abscesses and similar things. Provide it with whatever is necessary for each situation until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	 of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by right name "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and it happens in the same way that a break occurs in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is also similar to that of the arm, and the work is the same. And if the two bones are broken together, the leg bends in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	 And if the small bone is broken, it bends forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 And if the large bone is broken, there is great pain and it is visible; and it bends downwards.[Note: I am making an assumption that "li gros os" refers to one of the two bones in the leg, either mustelz or foscile. It is possible that "li gros os" could have a different meaning, as the text does not provide sufficient context.]
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Then apply traction and align it evenly, and bind the limbs equally; but if the fracture is severe and there are multiple pieces, the traction should be lighter; and adjust accordingly to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when you have completed your work, take two belts of woven wood that encircle the leg on both sides, and extend from the knee downwards; then wrap it in two layers above and below, and bind it in the middle so that the leg cannot decline to the right or left, and this is good. And some administer a splint made of wood that extends along the length of the leg, and place the leg on it to prevent movement. This is done properly in cases of fracture with wounds. Move the leg daily to check for signs of inflammation or other complications; treat until healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	 of the fracture of bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	 At the ankle there is no fracture, but sometimes the bones of the foot are fractured and also the toes, and there is nothing but multiple displacements (of the broken parts).
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	 And if it happens that there is a fracture in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones protruding over each other, then place the patient's foot on the ground, as if they were going to walk, and then place your foot on top of theirs where the bones are raised, then press down hard until they return to their places; then apply a plaster and bandages, and under the belly of the foot, place a small board two fingers wide, then bind it to the corresponding foot, after wrapping cloth around, and other things you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	 And when three or four days have passed, loosen the bandage, because you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	 And if some of the fingers are broken, set them right as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint on the broken finger according to the length of the finger, and make it a bit wider, then put beneath the foot the board that I mentioned, and bind it appropriately; and if there are two or three, or more, breaks, place a splint on each one according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the board beneath the foot; and let it extend over the belly of the foot so that it covers it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	 And you should not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, just as we have mentioned; and treat each accident as it is appropriate.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	 Of the fracture of the arm bone.
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bone of a woman's arm is broken, make her sit with her elbow extended, then lean her towards the back and support her from behind; fill a bowl with cotton and stuff it into the wound as much as possible, like a fist; then lift her arm and shoulder and let the cotton come out until it reaches the entrance of the wound, and the bone will return to its place with the cotton; when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and replace it after she is done for seven days or so: the fracture will be healed. And if you wish, take a bladder of grass, attach a cane to it, and insert the entire bladder into the wound; then blow hard into the cane until the bladder expands inside; the bone will return to its place, then fill it with cotton and leave it like that for several days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bone of the arm in a man or woman is broken, set it as we have said for the bone of the thigh; and such close fractures are not hidden from one who applies careful study and attention to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 For a fracture indicates in various ways the right path of restoration, so understand that.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	 In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's throat and insert the penis into it; then wrap it with cloth and leave it for three days or until it heals quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	 of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	 It is necessary for one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, to be healed immediately, just as the signs that we have mentioned testify.[NOTE: "sainie" in medieval medical texts can refer to various types of bodily fluids or discharges, including pus and blood. In this context, it seems to refer to the pus or other fluid that is drained from a wound as part of the healing process.]
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the wound is clean, staunch it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then begin to restore the broken bone in that same hour, or that day, unless abscesses appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	 And if abscesses appear, delay the restoration until the ninth day, until the abscess subsides, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause a harmful occurrence.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	 And if the broken bone appears above the skin uncovered, it is necessary that you gently align it with your hands, with slight extension.[Comment: I am not adding any comments or contextual information about the text as per your instructions, but just to let you know this translation seems accurate based on my understanding of Old French and medieval medical terminology.]
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	 And if the extensions are not ready for you to place evenly in your hands, then realign it with this instrument which is of iron, being 7 or 8 inches long, and its width is according to the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the surgeon to press III or IIII, as much as is needed in each fracture cure; and it should be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not bend during compression on the member while you are working, and it should be sharp at the tip, and thick from the middle towards the front, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called a "palancelle," for which reason the curved part must be placed on top of the visible end of the bone; and push it once, until it aligns, and make them even with each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot well grasp the bone, then you must cut the top of the bone, so that the instrument has power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	 And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument for this purpose, such as a knife or scalpel, to your ability; then scrape away at the roughness and small shavings that remain in the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position.[It is important to note that this translation is not necessarily accurate, as Old French is a complex language with many variations, and this text is written in an archaic style. However, I have done my best to provide an accurate and readable translation based on the given context and information.].
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 Make sure it is back in its place, then wet a cloth in black stiptic wine, and apply it properly if it's in the summer; and do not put any plaster or other oil-containing substance on the wound, as it may cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer cauterizing irons when you have set the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering to fit the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not constricted by the break; and many times foolish surgeons have made this mistake, causing either death or corruption in the patient; and the constraining force should be lighter and softer than for other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is large or bad, and you fear that evil accidents may occur, as we have said, and find pain in the place, then you should not at all apply cauterization; but instead, wrap hard bandages around it, in place of cauterization, and bind it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after one or two days the wound becoming swollen, remove what you have put on it and apply wound-healing ointment, such as tetrapharmacon ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	 And it is necessary to unbind the limb two times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and cured.[ barnacle geese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barnacle_goose)
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	 And it is necessary that the limb be aligned in such a way that the bone can easily slide down.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	 And if for many days it remains unset and can no longer join but the bone keeps protruding, know that there are small fragments of bone, therefore you must dress the wound with a tent and remove all the separated pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula comes to the place, or any other form of corruption, it should be treated according to what is said in the previous chapter.[
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, do not pull it out because many times it leads to death, but leave it until it rots; perhaps after twenty or thirty days it will come out by itself, then cure the wound if you can, and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	 of boils that come up on the skin
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	 We often see after the healing of a bursting (of an abscess), even when it is close to the joint, and it is an unpleasant sight, the appearance of the limb; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 Take notice then if the swelling comes to you: administer styptic medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla, acacia, and similar things, either one of these or all mixed together, and infuse with astringent wine or egg white or vinegar; and apply it to the swelling in linen rags, and bind it firmly, not loosening it for several days; then loosen it and begin another, until the swelling is removed; or you can tie it to a piece of well-made wood, for the property of wood is that it removes all swelling from the limbs; and if the swelling has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut it open and let the excess be apparent; or have it shaved by a skilled barber until it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	 the weakened limb after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	 When the fracture of the bone is healed, but the limb remains weak and fragile afterwards, it can happen for many reasons: one of which is that it was bound too tightly, and not as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, preventing blood flow to the limb; or due to excessive swelling; or due to excessive movement at the wrong time; or because there is little blood in its body, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	 And the treatment is that you should feed the patient and make the body supple so that blood multiplies within it; and administer baths to him, and give him joy and pleasure; then apply a poultice on the limb, such that the poultice draws out great moisture, and often rinse it with warm water until blood flow returns to the limb; and it regains its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	 twisted limb after the healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	 When a member is twisted after being set, and the bone is visibly broken, and the shape of the limb is misshapen, it does not lose its natural function; do not believe the foolish ones who say that the member should be broken again, many foolish surgeons have done this in our land; and these works are blamed, and great harm comes from it, even death; however, if the knots and tension are fresh, they should be soaked in hot water, or softening herbs should be cooked, such as leaves of mallow, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make a softening plaster, such as well-made daisy ointment, and take the crushed leaves of mallow, and preserve it with goose fat or oil of St. John's wort, and make a plaster of it; or take figs and crush them with cow dung, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes, the knots are removed by continuously and lengthily rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And make sure to ease the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	 And if the twisted parts are swollen and hardened, like stone, and need to be removed with iron, then it should be covered down to the bone, with a delicate incision using a lancet; and place cotton and bandage on the wound in treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	 Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	 Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.[8](https://www.ancientpages.com/2019/03/07/medieval-french-manuscript-offers-insight-into-13th-century-surgical-practices/)
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	 When a dislocation occurs, it must be corrected immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 For if one delays, the area swells, and perhaps it cannot be reset in its place; therefore, it should not be moved while it is swollen: often this brings on spasms and other pains; nonetheless, when this happens, let the patient take a laxative, then wait until the abscess has subsided; then apply warm water and oil to the affected area, then gently reset the limb, and treat each member as it returns to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	 And I have organized the chapters on dislocations from head to foot.
des mandibules	 of the lower jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	 It rarely happens that both jaws are dislocated, and there are two ways in which the dislocation of both occurs: either they are slightly out of place and somewhat loose; or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the chin, with saliva flowing from the mouth that he cannot hold, and is unable to close his mouth, and his tongue becomes entangled when speaking.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	 When the dislocation is small, it can return to its place through several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And if it is complete and full, then you must quickly reset it and not delay; and in such a way that the assistant holds the head of the patient, and places a small cloth with one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is two-sided; and with the other hand, he should provide equal pressure; and command the patient to relax, his jaws, and move them in all directions.[Instructions for resetting a complete jaw dislocation]
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	 And the physician places it evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the returning is difficult, even if it is the two jawbones assembled, soak them in hot water and oil, until you can easily reset them; do not delay the resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are evenly reset, and the patient's mouth closes well without difficulty, place wet bandages soaked in a mixture of rose oil and wax on it, then bind it lightly with soft ligaments; and let the patient sleep on their back, with their head resting between two pillows, so that it is not moved to the right or left, and they should not force themselves to chew, but eat light food until the pain is gone and the jawbones are healed; and then eat what they want lightly, and do not strain to open their mouth while eating and drinking, until the jawbones are fully healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	 And if the two jawbones cannot be set right within an hour, and are not restored to their place, then fevers and fixed abscesses will ensue, and perhaps digestive trouble, and perhaps vomiting of pus.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	 And when you see this, know that it is a lost cause; and many times death comes to those for whom it happens, within nine days.
de la forcelle	 of the forceps
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	 The forceps cannot be removed from the ribcage and the lung tissue without causing damage, and if it is removed it can be felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is as follows: let the patient lie flat on their back and extend their arms; then press firmly with your palm in that place and it will return; then apply the poultice and bandage, and bind it; and the side that is turned towards the cut cannot be removed; if it can, do so, and if it comes loose at any time, reset it as we have said; then apply the poultice and bandage, and bind it, and command the patient to rest until they are healed; and similarly, bring back the side of the shoulder blade when it has become dislocated from its place.[translation corrected on 2023-03-28]
de la dislocation de l’espaule	 of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder does not dislocate in any other way than three manners: of which one is that it dislocates at the side of the socket below; and the second is to the side of the hip; and perhaps it dislocates above, but this rarely happens; and it never dislocates backward for the shoulder, nor does it dislocate inside for the nerves; and often it dislocates downward toward the socket, especially in those who have little flesh, because it slips quickly in them; in those who have enough flesh, it slips less and returns less easily.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	 And perhaps it happens to some men that they have a percussion or a fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they believe that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	 Then you should try it, until you are certain; and only then should you begin the cure.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 A dislocation is recognized when it is lowered towards the shoulder blade, and there is a noticeable difference between the healthy and the injured shoulder, and you will find a depression on the shoulder's top, and under the shoulder blade when touching the chief of the shoulder, just like an abscess; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor make any movements; and also if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you can clearly feel it; and this type of dislocation is easy to correct when it's new or in case of a child.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	 And the manner is that the minister lifts the patient's hand up, then places their fingers under the affected area, and forcefully lifts the joint into place; and the minister lifts the hand, stretches it up, then puts it down; it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come as we have said in many days, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and they should be given a soothing and relaxing concoction, such as a decoction of althea, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and they should be massaged; then the patient should be propped up on their back, and put under the affected area a woolen cushion, neither too soft nor too hard, then place the physician's heel on the cushion, and lift the healthy shoulder forcefully, and pull the hand of the patient; and another minister holds the head of the patient so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder will come back into place immediately, and if you see that it is necessary to reset it in this manner: and that is that there be present a person who is larger than the patient; and they should stand at their side, and push their shoulder under the affected area of the patient, and lift the affected area upwards, so that the patient hangs from it; and another minister pulls down on the hand of the patient towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too lightweight, have them hold onto something heavy, and the dislocation will return to its place now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And the dislocation can also be reset in another way: first, insert a long stake into the ground so that the patient's head is as high as a fistful, and neither too thick nor too thin; then place it beneath the patient, with soft cloths on top, and have the patient lie lengthwise along the stake. Next, stretch out the affected limb away from the body and straighten it; the joint will quickly return to its proper position. If it still does not wish to return despite all of these measures, perform this cure: take a stake that is two arms' lengths long and four fingers wide, with a pointed end that can be inserted deeply beneath the dislocated bone as shown here.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	 then place the soft folded cloth on the patient's head, so that the stick does not injure or poke the patient, then place it under the patient's buttock; extend their arm on the long part of the stick, and tie the shoulder to the stick and the arm to the head of the hand, then place the arm on a rung of a wide ladder, and let the hands hang down, and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will return to its place now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	 And when it is back in place, in whatever manner, you should then place a roll of wool under the buttock, then apply a poultice that is equally prepared with powdered flour, incense and egg white, all over the shoulder and around it; then bind it appropriately under the buttock, and turn the bandage over the poultice, and embrace the hand to their neck, and let the hand remain in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	 And it is necessary that he eats little, until the limb is strengthened, for it will heal more quickly; and then eat more after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for another reason, then you should apply cautery to it at three points, as it is described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	 And if you do all this, and after 7 days it becomes dislocated again, and the joint cannot hold and the arm cannot be lifted up, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The dislocation that is toward the side of the hip, and the breasts, or the back, is made by impact and extension of the hands, and another limb is used to treat it; and one must take care of it until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	 And if after the healing comes cracking in the limb, and slowness in movement, then the patient should take many baths until the cracking is relieved and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	 of the dislocation of the ribcage[ (my interpretation based on context) ]
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	 Know that the joint of the ribcage is dislocated at points and returns to those same points, and it is dislocated all around, including both front and back, and the dislocation is not reset because it is visible and can be felt; and it is dislocated according to each figure (shape/position).
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the sharp knife with the vein, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 Because the joint is dislocated and cannot bend the arm or touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	 And you must reset it in such a way that abscesses will not form there, because if abscesses do form, it would be difficult to reset; and perhaps it cannot be fully reset, especially when it is located in the back; this type of dislocation is worse than others, and causes greater pain, and possibly death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	 And the restoration is, when it is in such a condition that it can be reset, to stretch out his hand with both of your hands; and let his arms be extended, and his hands over and under, around the knife, and push the joint back into place at its ends, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its original position.[imagine prompt: A medieval doctor restoring a dislocated arm]
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	 And if the dislocation is in front, it comes back when he bends his arm at the elbow, and strikes the root of the palm with the displaced joint.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 And if it does not want to return to its place, then strong extension is administered; and this is done by two people extending the arm, and holding it with two hands so that it does not move during the extension. Then bend the arm from both sides after you have wrapped a long and wide cloth around it. And when the surgeon has aligned the joint to the hand, he anoints it with some oil to soften the joint, then forcefully push the joint until it returns; and when it is in place, put dry ointment with egg white on it, and hold it firmly, and bend the arm over the patient's neck, and leave it like that for a few days, then loosen it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	 And if the joint is tight in its place, loosen the ligament and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not fitting well, reapply the poultice and the ligament, and leave it for several days until it is firmly in place; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if it feels tight after the resetting of the joint and it moves, bathe and gently rub it, pressing until it is relieved; or place a sheep's fat icese on the joint, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it and have them enter the bath; and when they sweat, gently rub the joint, then replace the icese and re-enter the bath; and do this twice or three times, until it is healed; and if you wish, place moist warm cow dung with butter on it, and bind it on; it will return to its normal position.
li dislocation de la main	 the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	 The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the recovery is easy, more so than other joints. Nevertheless, it should be quickly returned to its place in the same hour that it is dislocated, so that the area swells or a hot abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 And the resetting is as follows: place the afflicted hand on a table, and extend it. The assistant should hold it evenly, and the physician should align it so that his palm is on the appearance of the joint, pushing until it returns to its place. Nevertheless, one must make sure that it is in the correct position; then, let the patient lay the back of their hand on a table for extension and resetting.[](https://french.stackexchange.com/)
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of his hand on the table, and let the doctor put his hand on the aforementioned part of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it (the dislocation) returns now, that is good. If not, bind it with soothing plasters for abscesses and leave it alone without moving it.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if he (the patient) cannot bear it and you are unable to set it in place after several days, then let the joint remain dislocated; and it will harm the patient only while his hand is swollen and he cannot move it at all: know that the nerves or arteries are cut. In such a case, there is no other remedy but to cauterize near the injury, and perhaps this will be of some help.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	 And when the hand is in place, apply the ointment that we mentioned, then bind it and leave it for 5 days, then unbind it and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he cannot move it well, and there is any cracking, wet it with warm water and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	 of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand dislocate on both sides, sometimes at the back of the palm or the belly; then straighten the finger and push the dislocation back into its place until it is set, then hold the top of the finger and bend it towards the side where it is disjointed; and leave it for 2 days, and then align it that day; and do not bind it, as we have said, and untie it every day and make it move, and rebind it at night; and do this frequently until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	 of the dislocation of the small of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	 When the small of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, for death is swift for the patient.
