Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the sign is that the patient urinates uncontrollably, unable to hold it in, and often certain limbs become weakened, or both thighs or arms or one; and frequently the small of the back moves in four ways; if the one that moves at the back is present, it is called "gilbositez"; the cure is to determine if "gilbositez" has come from infancy: if so, there is no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And the one who has just fallen or been struck or by similar things, ancient methods of cures said in grand words, which do not bring great benefit in all cases; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have fashioned instruments in diverse ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the gout that comes to the front of the foot, there is no device nor health; and also the one that comes directly between two ribs, and it cannot be cured except by the very same one that comes on the back, as I am saying; and it is necessary for the patient to be stretched out on their back evenly, and have support beneath them so they do not injure themselves; then insert a stake in the ground at the head and another at the feet, and tie a rope underneath the patient's ankles and also around their calves, knees, and ankles; and two assistants must know the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two stakes; and they should be tightened well, as we have said, and the attendant should place their palms firmly on the affected area until it feels better.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if it does not return to its place with this treatment, take a board of three arms' length, shaved underneath, and let the patient be on his side, and put the head of the board under the opening, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and have the doctor put his feet on the other end of the board and press hard until it returns to its place; and if you wish, do it with a device that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And it is that you drive two stakes into the head of the patient, one of a large arm's length and the other towards the feet, and have between each stake, above and below, a palm's space in length; and have in each stake one hole where the device turns, and let the stakes be firmly in the ground so that they do not move; and between each pair of stakes have one turning stake, on which the ropes turn, and have in two turnings two small stakes of a palm's length, to turn the device; and then tie the rope that is between the saddle to the device towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet to the other device, and each assistant turns his device to the full extent of the rope, and the master puts the spine in alignment as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it is aligned, place a desiccative emplaster with plenty of egg yolk on it, then the wadding, then an elongated stylet of three fingers' length from a tablet, which reaches the area of the gouty inflammation and the healthy part of the shoulder blade, then bind it with a ligature as we have said, and have the patient use gentle exercise until it is healed; and if any issue arises at the end of the healing process, laxative and soothing medicines should be administered along with the previously mentioned stylet; and sometimes a piece of plastic is administered, and sometimes an appearance arises in the lower shoulder blade of the back, and it is thought to be a dislocation; but it is actually the bone that appears, for which one must not make assumptions: perhaps it could bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	 of dislocations of the hip joint
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	 Know that the joints of the hip and shoulder do not dislocate like other joints, but rather only dislocate; and the joint of the hip can become dislocated in four ways: inward, outward, forward, and backward; and more often inward than outward, and less so forward and backward.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the recognition of its inward dislocation is as follows: when joining the sick leg with the healthy one, it appears longer, and the affected knee appears more open than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee over the fire; and the area next to it is swollen due to an abscess because the thigh muscle has come there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	 And the sign of that person who becomes affected by it, is that these symptoms are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	 And the sign of the one who becomes affected (by dislocation), is that they can stretch their leg according to its normal length; yet, they cannot bend the knee without pain, and if made to walk, they cannot move forward, and they hold their urine, and their ankle swells, and when they walk, they tread on their heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	 And the sign of the one who becomes affected (by dislocation) in the back, is that they cannot stretch or bend their knee, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and their ankle is loose, and the head of the femur is out of place under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	 The reduction of such a similar dislocation is as follows: you should examine if the dislocation is old, and if it stays in its place according to its disposition, in which case there is no need for treatment; and one should not be overconfident.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	 And for the one with a fresh dislocation, which is one of the four types of dislocations, you should quickly return the joint to its place, stretch it inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return to its place, and there is no need for further treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this manner, then you should prepare for a strong minister and hold the leg with two hands, or tie it with a ligament above the knee; and another minister extends his hand above in such a way that he places his hands beneath the patient's heels, then squeezes him gently with a soft ligament on the thigh; and another holds the patient's head with the ligament; and they all stretch upwards and downwards at once, so that the patient is raised from the ground once and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	 This method of stretching is common to four similar instances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 If not, care must be taken in the same manner when the dislocation is on the side. One should lay the patient on their healthy side, then place a bandage on the root of the thigh and the area beneath the groin. Next, pull the bandage up towards the groin and the hip; then have another assistant take hold of the patient's arms and embrace the large part of the affected thigh, extending it outward strongly. The dislocation will return to its place in this manner; this type of dislocation is easier than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot pull it (the dislocation) back in this manner as we have said, then you should tie the patient's two feet together with a strong soft ligature at the heels and at the knees, and let the affected leg be extended two fingers more than the other; then let him hang by a beam over his head, and let there be two arms length from the ground; then command a minister to embrace the thigh's head, and let there be another minister hanging with the patient, who firmly embraces the thigh, for the joints return quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And when the dislocation is out of place, let the patient lie down as we have said in the one with gout, and tighten the ligature on the affected leg properly, and on the foot as well; then put two sticks, one at the head and one at the feet, then stick one stick between the patient's thighs in the middle; and have a dressing of wet rags around it so that it does not wound the patient, then each minister stretches out towards him, and let the physician place his hand evenly on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it comes back, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, place it on a table and press it as we have said in gilbosité, and let the patient lie on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	 And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to quickly stretch out the sick leg as I have said, and make an effort to be on the sick ankle, then press with the other hand and pull down towards the knee.[--------------------------------------------------------](https://www.reddit.com/r/AskLinguistics/comments/u8z2m3/comment/i5n960e/?utm_source=share&utm_medium=web2x&context=3)
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is on the outside, it is not necessary to stretch out the sick part downward or lift it off the ground. Instead, it should be as if the swelling was on the outside, as we have said about lying on two heels. Let them lie on their back and the bandages stretched out as we have said before, and press on the joint against the table. It is done when the patient stretches their legs and they are even. Then adjust the hips, apply the poultice, and bind it with a bandage so that the swelling does not move. Let it rest for three or four days, then loosen it and apply the poultice again. If you see that they are even, bind it as before and let it rest for three days. Then loosen it and make them walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	 of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	 The knee dislocates in three ways: namely, inward and outward, and backward; it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at their hip, and if they cannot do so, know that it is dislocated; and the treatment for all of them is to have the patient sit upright, extend their leg if they can, and place your back against their thigh, and put their foot on your feet; then take their knee in your palms, and pull it out between your fingers, then forcefully bend the two sides of the knee; and another assistant should stretch the person's foot until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that they can easily bend their leg at their hip; and apply a compress and heat the leg against the hip, and bind them tightly together for three or four days, then loosen it; and the patient should not move or walk until the limb has been strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not aligned, stretch it strongly, as we have said in the treatment of inflammation, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	 Of the ankle dislocation.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	 The heels are sometimes dislocated, and at other times completely dislodged, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and it tilts towards the side where it is dislocated. The resetting is easy, and it should be gently stretched with one's hands when only dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is dislocated completely, you must make the patient sit upright, and hold them by the leg above the ankle with two ministers (assistants). Then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards, and place the foot in its proper position. Do this twice, as we have said, by pulling and stretching the foot. If it returns to its original position, that is good. If not, then repeat the process, for it will return. And if it cannot be returned using this method, then make the patient lie down on their back on the ground, and firmly plant a stake in the ground between their thighs and tie a cloth around it so as not to injure the patient. Then hold the thigh with one minister, and another stretches the foot with their hands or with a strap tied around the shin. Each minister should then pull evenly, while the stake holds the patient down. The physician should then place both hands on the dislocation, and another minister holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will quickly return to its original position.[Important note: This translation is for educational purposes only and should not be used as medical advice. It describes outdated medical practices that are not in line with modern medicine.]
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it is ready, put the poultice and wadding on, and bind it firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the bandage is not too tight; then leave it for 2 or 3 days, and if the bandage loosens, bind it again; then untie it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient to walk for 4 days; and if he goes before this term, it is not certain that he will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if an abscess comes to a head, you should soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	 of the arms/wrists
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	 When the two (arms/wrists) are dislocated, they should be stretched out nicely without force, and this is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back or leg, you should have the patient sit upright on a level surface or table, and place your foot on top of the affected joints. Then press firmly with your foot until it returns to its normal position, and once it's even and there is nothing protruding, place a two-legged table under the sole of your foot and apply strong pressure, leaving it in place for three days before releasing. Allow it to rest until it has healed.[Note: This translation is intended to be as literal as possible and may not make complete sense in English.]
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	 of wound and of dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When wound comes with dislocation, and one wants to heal it, often the patient dies if you are presumptuous in treatment, if you are not wise in the art or have not practiced long, and if you are not compassionate and merciful, slow but not hasty. At the beginning, use soothing remedies for the abscess, keep the patient in God's hands if there is no hope of health, and when there is hope, reset the limb to its place as long as the abscess subsides. Once the limb is set, administer soothing remedies for the abscess, treat the wound appropriately with drying ointments, and if the dislocation comes with a fracture and displaced small bones, remove them and do what we have said in simple illnesses. Be cautious about entering the path of fear as I have mentioned, for it will harm you according to your Creator, and protect your equipment and body.
Amen	 Amen
